# Rogue — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# Executive Brief (BLUF)

## Bottom Line, Up Front

Subject is a woman organized, root to crown, around a single biological fact: **the channel through which human beings give and receive non-verbal proof that they are loved — skin-to-skin affective touch — is, for her, the channel through which she harms.** Every other feature of her presentation, from the cultivated Mississippi-belle vocal register down to the granular choice of glove length and seam placement, is a derivative of that fact. She is not, at depth, a "tragic mutant" in the romantic register the team's press materials prefer. She is a person living with an exceptionally well-characterized chronic deprivation injury (Sailer et al., 2016, *NeuroImage* 139:360–367 — orbitofrontal cortex and putamen recruitment by C-tactile afferent input; reward-circuit substrate of bonding) on top of two index traumas (the Cody Robbins coma; the Carol Danvers absorption) and a developmentally disorganizing childhood (paternal flight; foster-rearing by a shapeshifter and a precognitive — caregivers who could not be visually trusted and from whom the child could not visually hide). The adaptation built on this substrate is, by clinical standards, **unusually successful**: she is durable, loyal past reason, capable of leadership, and — the rarest pro-social marker in the file — she walks *toward* the people she has wronged rather than away from them. The file should not be read as a portrait of pathology. It is a portrait of an exceptionally hard-won functional equilibrium maintained against continuous biological headwind.

## The Through-Line of the Entire Existence

A single vector runs from Caldecott County to the Quiet Council and does not deviate: **the search for a containing object that can hold her without being destroyed.** Read longitudinally, every major decision in sixty years of published life resolves onto this vector.

- The pre-manifestation flight from the paternal household: the first containing object failed; she left.
- The acceptance of Mystique-and-Destiny as foster parents: a second container offered itself; she took it, ideology included, because containment was the scarce good.
- The Cody Robbins kiss: the first attempt to extend the container to a peer; catastrophic failure encoded the conditioned stimulus class (touch → harm → irreversibility) that governs the rest of her life.
- The Danvers assault: under Mystique's ideological frame, she attempted to *take* containment by force — to absorb a whole adult woman's competence, confidence, and self — and discovered she had committed, in effect, a psychic murder. This is the wound that drives the reparation engine for the next four decades.
- The unannounced arrival at Xavier's door (*Uncanny X-Men* #171, 1983): the defining pro-social act. She walked toward the parties with most reason to kill her, because they were the only ones who might hold her without being destroyed by what was inside her. The pattern recurs across her life: **she seeks rescue from the people she has wronged.** This is structurally healthy and statistically rare.
- The Gambit courtship: selection of the one available partner whose own concealment matched hers, whose charm-as-armor mirrored hers, and whose pre-existing moral debts made him unable to demand purity from her. The relationship is, in attachment terms, a brilliantly chosen developmental experiment.
- The Siege Perilous walk-through (*Uncanny X-Men* #247): the through-line briefly inverted — when containment seemed impossible, she chose ego-erasure as relief. The fact that she *returned* and reconsolidated is, retrospectively, the single most prognostically favorable datum in the file.
- The Carey-era power integration arc (*X-Men: Legacy*): the first time the literal obstacle to containment was therapeutically addressed rather than narratively endured. The fact that her first use of controlled touch was *protective contact with teammates in combat* rather than romantic consummation tells you exactly where her priority structure sits.
- The marriage (*Mr. and Mrs. X*, 2018): the through-line's first sustained consummation. Achieved only after the medical obstacle was provisionally solved — i.e., she would not permit herself the goal until the structural risk to the other party was acceptable. This is conscience, not avoidance.
- The Quiet Council seat (Krakoan era): the through-line's terminal move so far. Having spent forty years seeking a container, she has become one — for the entire nation. The arc from "child who could not be held" to "person who holds the polity" is the cleanest pro-social trajectory in the file.

The vector does not waver. It only matures.

## The Core Wound and Its Maintenance

**The core wound is not the Cody event and not the Danvers event.** Those are the index traumas — the moments at which the wound's *content* was filled in. The wound itself is structural and prior: **she was raised by caregivers whose faces could not be trusted as data** (Mystique's shapeshifting, Destiny's precognitive omniscience), in a household where the child was never accurately mirrored back to herself and was always being seen through rather than seen. Onto that pre-existing identity-diffusion substrate, the mutation arrived and operationalized the wound at the level of the skin: she now cannot let anyone close enough to mirror her without absorbing them and proving, again, that what is inside her is dangerous to what is outside her.

**Maintenance mechanisms — why the wound persists despite four decades of corrective experience:**

1. *Biological reinforcement.* The deprivation is not psychological. The C-tactile afferent reward channel (Sailer et al., 2016) is genuinely offline. No amount of cognitive reframing closes a sensory-reward gap. Every day not touched is a day of unmet biological need, and the need does not habituate.
2. *The countermeasure is the symptom.* Gloves and full coverage are simultaneously medical necessity and characterological armor. She cannot remove the armor without endangering others; therefore the defense cannot be relinquished even in the safest possible setting. This is an unusually punishing structural feature: most defenses can in principle be put down. Hers cannot.
3. *Reaction-formation surface.* The "sugah," the flirtation, the Southern-belle warmth — these are the overproduced surface markers of affect she cannot deliver in the body. The surface works socially, which means it is reinforced continuously, which means the gap between surface warmth and substrate deprivation is renewed every interaction.
4. *Mystique, permanently.* The maternal transference cannot be metabolized because the maternal object will not stay still long enough to be metabolized — literally. Every time subject approaches closure with Mystique, Mystique becomes someone else, and the work resets.
5. *Absorbed-psyche residue.* Each major absorption (Danvers, Magneto, Gambit's Marauder history, many others) deposits material in the substrate that subject must then re-sort into self / not-self. The fear is permanent: *is there a coherent me underneath the inputs?* This is the deepest interrogable anxiety in the file.
6. *Reparation as renewable fuel.* The guilt over Danvers is hyperactive, not absent. It funds the pro-social labor that defines her adult life. The wound is *useful* — and a useful wound resists closure. The X-Men tenure metabolizes guilt into work; if the guilt closed, the work might too.

## Operational Summary

**Disposition.** Pragmatic operator; loyalist; reliable under fire to a degree that exceeds her own stated estimate of herself. Will take physical and psychic punishment to spare a teammate. Will absorb a hostile combatant knowing the psychic blowback is hers to carry afterward. This willingness is not heroism in the bravado register — it is the reparation engine running on combat fuel.

**Cognitive style.** Concrete, fast, accurate read of people (partly trained by Mystique, partly the residue of having been literally inside other minds). Not intellectual; not anti-intellectual; bored by mysticism, alert to ideology. Underestimates her own analytic capacity and is underestimated by others on the same grounds — her presentation cues "Southern charm operator," her output is "Council-grade strategist."

**Affect under load.** Surface heat (temper, sass, combative humor) is a controlled-release valve. Tears are rare and hydraulic when they come. Decompensation pathway is well-characterized: absorbed-psyche intrusion → dissociative displacement → identification with the donor → requires external psychic intervention to recover. She is most dangerous **to herself**, not to others, when destabilized.

**Stress signatures.** Under acute stress, the two surface defenses spike together — *more* physically aggressive and *more* flirtatiously verbal in the same minute. Under chronic stress, the geographic-flight pattern engages (the recurring "Rogue leaves the team" beat across the publication record). Under existential stress, ego-erasure has been tabled at least once.

**Exploitable pressure points** (file these for awareness, not use):
- Any framing that invokes the Danvers act.
- Mystique, in any guise, at any range.
- Threats to Gambit specifically; threats to the marriage structurally.
- Touch-temptation scenarios (a hostile telepath could weaponize the deprivation directly).
- The accusation that she is not a coherent self underneath the absorbed inputs.

**Stabilizing anchors** (the corresponding asset side):
- Storm (durable sister/maternal substitute; the only early authority who held).
- Gambit (load-bearing relational structure of the current self).
- Institutional role (the Quiet Council seat externalizes the containing-object function; *being* the container reduces the pressure of *seeking* one).
- Mentorship of younger mutants (produces, in the next generation, the secure attachment she did not receive — a clean displacement of the deprivation into pro-social output).
- Combat (paradoxically regulating; sanctioned contact-through-fabric is the closest legal approximation of the affective input she is denied).

**Trust calibration.** Trustworthy at the level of action and loyalty without qualification. Trustworthy at the level of self-report with one caveat: she chronically under-reports her own suffering and over-reports her own culpability. Any debrief should weight her affective self-assessment downward and her behavioral record upward.

**Operational ceiling.** Higher than the early file suggests and probably higher than she herself believes. The trajectory from Brotherhood foot-soldier to Council seat is not a redemption arc in the sentimental sense — it is a forty-year demonstration that an originally pathological guilt, harnessed to a durable temperament and a chosen institutional frame, produces unusually competent adult functioning. Prognosis: **stable, with predictable destabilizers**, all of which are known and most of which are avoidable.

**Bottom line of the bottom line.** A person whose body forbids the thing her psyche most needs; who was raised by caregivers she could not visually trust; who in adolescence committed an act she has spent her adult life repaying; who chose, against the odds, to walk toward the people she had wronged; who built a marriage, a command, and a self on top of a biological deprivation that does not abate. The wound is permanent. The person built on top of it is the file's principal finding.


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD

*Subject: ROGUE — Anna Marie (legal surname inconsistent in record; "Raven" by adoption-of-record; "LeBeau" by current marriage; the birth surname is intentionally suppressed in the published canon, which is itself a datum — see §1.2 below). File-section covers the period from birth through the manifestation of the X-gene at approximately age thirteen and the immediate aftermath in the Darkholme/Adler household.*

---

## 1.1 Birth, Geography, and the Caldecott County Substrate

**Place of birth: Caldecott County, Mississippi** (Claremont, *Uncanny X-Men* #178, 1984; expanded in flashback throughout the 1980s; reiterated *Rogue* vol. 3 #1–12, Robert Rodi, 2004, which returns subject physically to the Caldecott parish to confront the origin terrain). Caldecott is a fictional Mississippi parish in the Claremont geography — swamp-edged, rural, evangelical Protestant, economically thin, sparsely populated. The published cues consistently code it as: pine and cypress, two-lane blacktop, a small white-frame house set back from a road, a porch, dogs, fundamentalist Christianity at the social baseline, and a near-total absence of the secular/cosmopolitan apparatus (no library culture, no peers from outside the county, no exposure to mutant discourse). The accent that subject retains across forty publication-years — a slow, vowel-dropped Mississippi cadence with the characteristic *sugah*, *darlin'*, *honeychile*, *Ah'm fixin' tuh* — is *not* affected; it is the linguistic fossil of the Caldecott childhood and one of the most stable behavioral markers in the file (it persists through Brotherhood years, X-Men years, Antarctic isolation, Krakoan governance — even when she is consciously code-switching for tactical purposes, the substrate accent surfaces under fatigue, intoxication-by-absorption, or affective load).

**Date of birth: deliberately obscured in canon.** Marvel's editorial convention floats her between ~13 and ~14 at manifestation and uses an indeterminate-young-adult age band through the Claremont, Lobdell, Carey, Thompson, and Duggan runs. The dossier treats the *vagueness itself* as the relevant fact: subject does not publicly mark birthdays, does not refer to her natal date, does not commemorate the natal year — consistent with the wider behavioral pattern of suppressed origin-data (see §1.2).

**Family of origin — paternal household.** The biological father (named in the post-Claremont expansion of the backstory, most fully in *Rogue* vol. 3 and *X-Men Origins: Gambit/Rogue* one-shots) is rendered as: working-class, religiously rigid, emotionally austere, alcohol-adjacent in the Southern-rural manner without being canonically a documented drunk, given to harsh corrective discipline, and bereaved. The biological mother (referred to as Priscilla in some expansions) is absent during the formative period — variously rendered as deceased, vanished into the Far Banks (the Cherokee-spirit-realm material introduced in *Rogue* vol. 3, which though tonally divisive is now in record), or simply gone. The operative fact for the file is *maternal absence from earliest memory.* Subject was raised without a mother in the home. There is a paternal aunt — Carrie — who appears in the *Rogue* vol. 3 material as the figure who actually fed and bathed the child after the mother's loss; subject's relationship to Aunt Carrie is the only canonically warm pre-mutation tie. Carrie is older, taciturn, churchgoing, and not equipped to interpret a child with a runaway temperament.

**Siblings: none documented.** Subject is an only child by record. This matters: she had no peer-witness inside the home, no co-traumatized sibling to corroborate, no younger sibling to protect-and-thereby-organize-around. The early identity-formation is therefore solitary inside the household and dependent on extra-household figures (Aunt Carrie, and later — catastrophically — Mystique).

## 1.2 The Suppression of the Birth Name

The file's single most diagnostic origin-datum is **the suppression of the legal birth surname.** Across four decades of publication, subject is "Anna Marie" — given name and middle name only — or "Rogue," her codename. Even on the Krakoan resurrection rolls (Hickman/Duggan era), even in the *Mr. and Mrs. X* marriage documents, the legal name renders as "Anna Marie" with the surname structurally vague or substituted (Darkholme by adoptive convention; LeBeau by marriage). This is not editorial oversight — it is a *forty-year-consistent character choice.* Subject does not name herself after her father. The suppression is the earliest, most durable act of self-authorship in the record: before she had a mutation, before she had a codename, she had already decided that the surname she was born under would not survive her into adulthood. Read forward, this anticipates the entire pattern — chosen family over given family, constructed identity over assigned identity, the codename "Rogue" itself (a self-applied label connoting unattached, ungovernable, off-the-grid) — and read backward, it indexes a household whose name was felt as something to be cast off rather than carried.

## 1.3 The Pre-Mutation Behavioral Baseline (~age 6 through ~age 13)

From the flashback record (Claremont, *Uncanny X-Men* #182, #185, the "Lost in the Funhouse" psychic-tour material in #265–269; Lobdell flashbacks in *X-Men* vol. 2 #41 and #44; the Rodi *Rogue* vol. 3 arc; the various *X-Men Origins* and *X-Men Unlimited* shorts; and the Carey-era reconstructions in *X-Men: Legacy* #224–230 when Rogue's mind is mapped), the following pre-mutation behavioral patterns can be reconstructed with confidence:

**Tomboy presentation.** Subject is repeatedly shown pre-manifestation in overalls, boots, hair loose or in a single plait, climbing, running, on the edge of woodland. She does not present as a Southern-belle child despite the cultural setting; the belle register is later, performed, and selectively deployed (see §1.7 on the accent-as-performance vs. accent-as-substrate distinction). The pre-mutation child is muddy, fast, and physically fearless.

**Animal affinity.** Strong, consistent. Dogs appear in nearly every Caldecott flashback; subject is shown crouched with hounds, riding horses (the equestrian thread is reinforced in the Mississippi-return material), tracking and identifying wildlife. The animal-tie is the *only pre-mutation form of cross-body intimacy* that the record preserves — and crucially, it survives the mutation, because animal touch is mediated through fur, hide, and the bodysuit. This is why every era of the file shows Rogue gravitating to non-human contact (the recurring horse-riding beats, the cat-and-dog presence in any domestic scene she occupies, the comfort she shows with Lockheed and other animal-coded teammates). The pattern starts here.

**Solitary play; runaway proclivity.** The record establishes — repeatedly — that subject ran away from home *before* her mutation activated. Distance and duration escalate across the pre-mutation years: first the back acreage, then the woods, then the county road, then overnight absences, then the runaway proper that puts her in Mystique's path. The runaway behavior is the load-bearing pre-mutation pattern. It tells the file two things: (a) the home environment was experienced as intolerable in advance of any mutant-related event, and (b) subject's coping strategy for intolerable affect was *geographic flight* — a pattern that recurs across every subsequent decade (Antarctic abandonment of Gambit, *X-Men* #45; the recurring "Rogue leaves the team" beats in the Lobdell, Claremont-redux, and Carey runs; the periodic Mississippi-return arcs).

**Religious exposure without religious internalization.** Caldecott Protestantism is in the air she breathes; church attendance is implied by setting; but subject as an adult shows *moral substrate* (responsibility, guilt, reparation, the conviction that actions have weight) without *doctrinal commitment* (no prayer behavior in the file, no scripture citation, no church-going as an X-Man, no priest-figure recourse even at peak crisis). The pattern fits a child who absorbed the ethical frame of fundamentalist Protestantism through ambient exposure and rejected its metaphysics by adolescence. This is consistent with the runaway trajectory: a child who is leaving the church-and-father package wholesale.

**Hyper-vigilance to adult mood.** Inferred from the speed and accuracy of her later interpersonal reads, and from the typical developmental pattern of children in austere, unpredictable paternal households. Subject reads rooms quickly — a skill the file documents across every era — and the foundation of that skill is pre-mutation, pre-Mystique, pre-Brotherhood. It was trained at home.

**No documented pre-mutation peer attachments.** No childhood friend appears in the record. No name from the Caldecott school years is preserved in canon. No first-crush figure before Cody Robbins. This is a substantial absence: forty years of flashbacks have produced no Caldecott peer the subject remembers warmly. Either the writers have neglected to invent one (possible) or — the file's working interpretation — the rural-isolation-plus-austere-household combination produced a child whose peer life was thin enough that no figure rose to flashback-worthiness. The first peer-with-affect in her life is the boy she put in a coma.

## 1.4 The Father: Functional Profile

Reconstructing from the runaway evidence, the religious-austere environmental cues, the maternal absence, the Aunt Carrie buffer role, and the lifelong suppression of the surname:

**The paternal household was experienced as unsafe enough to flee but not violent enough to leave canonical injury markers.** Subject does not present with the somatic signatures of a physically battered child (no flinch-response to raised hands documented; no scar narrative; no PTSD-style startle keyed to male voices specifically). The injury was almost certainly *emotional and disciplinary austerity, religiously framed, in the context of grief* — a father who had lost a wife, did not know how to raise a daughter, and substituted rules and distance for parenting. The runaway behavior is the appropriate child-response to that environment: not escape from beating, but escape from a house in which she was unseen, unwelcomed, and unheld.

**The father is structurally absent from her adult life.** No documented adult reunion. No deathbed scene (in baseline continuity). No reconciliation arc. He functions in the dossier as the *negative space* from which she ran. The relevant fact is not what he did but that subject never returned to find out, and never built an adult relationship with him — the only paternal-transference figures in her adult record are Xavier (tentative, abandoned), Magneto (charged, romantic-coded, rejected after exposure to madness), and her acceptance of Gambit's father-figure Jean-Luc post-marriage. The biological father is the void those substitutes are arranged around.

## 1.5 The Cody Robbins Event (~age 13)

**The triggering incident** (Claremont, *Uncanny X-Men* #182, 1984; reiterated and expanded in numerous flashbacks, most pointedly *Uncanny X-Men* #269, *X-Men* vol. 2 #24, and the Carey *X-Men: Legacy* mind-tour issues #224–229).

Cody Robbins is a Caldecott boy, peer-aged, by the record a friend or a familiar figure rather than a stranger — the kiss is canonical first-kiss material, not assault, not random encounter, not coerced. The scene is rendered consistently across writers: a quiet outdoor setting, two adolescents, a first kiss attempted with the ordinary nervousness of first kisses. Subject's mutation activates *at the moment of skin contact at the lips.* She cannot release. By the time she pulls away, Cody is unconscious. He does not wake. He remains comatose for years (the canon eventually closes the loop — Cody appears as a coma victim in *X-Men* #24 and as a deceased figure in later flashbacks).

**The behavioral imprint of this single event organizes the rest of the file.**

- *First intimate act of her life produced catastrophic harm.* The conditioning trial is perfect: the conditioned stimulus (intimate touch) produced the unconditioned response (the other person collapses). No subsequent therapy or relationship can fully extinguish a learning trial this clean.
- *The harm was to a peer of the gender she was oriented toward.* Heterosexual romantic intimacy is therefore the specific axis along which the trauma is encoded. (The later courtship with Gambit takes its excruciating tempo from exactly this — every approach toward kissing him reactivates the Cody learning trial.)
- *The harm was witnessed by no one and confessed to no one in the household.* The runaway followed almost immediately. Subject did not have a parent to bring the crisis to. There was no adult interpretive frame imposed on the event before she fled. This is the origin of her lifelong pattern of *carrying central traumas privately* — she did not learn to bring catastrophe to an attachment figure because there was no attachment figure to bring it to.
- *The body became the weapon.* From this moment forward, subject's relationship to her own skin is adversarial. The bodysuit-as-prosthetic (see medical §2) is the somatic externalization of an inner conviction formed in this incident: *my body is a danger to the people I love.*
- *The runaway was overdetermined.* She was already running before; now she had a reason that could not be returned from.

## 1.6 The Encounter with Mystique and Destiny; the Foster Household

**Recruitment.** Mystique (Raven Darkholme) and Destiny (Irene Adler) find the runaway adolescent — exact mechanism varies by retelling but consistently: Mystique recognizes the mutant signature, Destiny has foreseen the arrival, the two of them take her in. The foster arrangement is formalized (Mystique becomes legal-adoptive in the Darkholme sense; Destiny is co-parent in fact if not in document; the lesbian-domestic structure of the household is now explicit canon following the post-2010s un-coding of the relationship, most fully in *X-Men: Bloodline* and the Hickman-Duggan-Ewing-era Krakoan rehabilitation of Destiny).

**The foster household — operational profile.**

- *Two mothers, one of whom can wear any face, the other of whom can see every outcome.* The phenomenological inheritance of this is profound and largely unrecognized in non-clinical readings of the character. Subject's primary caregivers were (a) a shapeshifter — the maternal face was literally non-constant; the child could not rely on visual recognition as a stable channel — and (b) a precognitive — the child was *seen through* (her futures known) rather than *seen* (her present known and held). The combination produces a uniquely warped mirroring environment. There is no stable face to imprint on; there is no felt sense of being a surprise to one's mother. Mystique is everywhere and nowhere; Destiny is always already ahead of you.
- *Affection was real.* Both Mystique and Destiny canonically loved Anna Marie. The household was warm in a way the paternal household was not — meals, conversation, instruction, physical care (within the still-pre-mutation early period; touch restrictions postdate Cody). This is critical: Mystique is not the cold villain-mother of cliché. Subject was, for the first time in her life, *wanted.* That the wanting came packaged with ideological recruitment and operational training does not retroactively void the affection. The file must hold both facts.
- *Moral pedagogy was inverted.* Mystique trained subject in infiltration, deception, combat, the use of cover identities, and the moral framework that mutants are at war with humanity and ordinary ethics do not apply to combatants in that war. Subject absorbed the combat-and-tradecraft competence (which has served her for forty years of publication) and the ideological framework (which she has spent forty years repudiating, except in the recurring crises when Mystique reactivates it).
- *Destiny's specific role.* The precognitive co-mother is the under-examined figure. Destiny *knew* the futures — she knew the Carol Danvers absorption would happen, she knew the X-Men defection would happen, she likely knew the marriage to Gambit would happen. The file's reading: Destiny loved Anna Marie with the particular weight of a parent who knows her child's coming injuries and does not (cannot, will not) prevent them. Subject's lifelong tolerance for being *known* — by telepaths, by absorbed psyches, by the Quiet Council's hyper-transparent governance — has its origin in being raised by a woman who already knew everything. Destiny's death (and later Krakoan resurrection) is felt by subject as a load-bearing loss in a way the file should not under-weight.
- *Caldecott was renounced; not erased.* The accent stayed. The Protestantism-substrate ethics stayed. The animal-affinity stayed. The runaway pattern stayed. Mystique gave her a new household but could not overwrite the substrate. This is why the adult Rogue presents as such a structurally legible person despite the chaos of her formation: the Caldecott layer is intact under the Brotherhood layer under the X-Men layer under the Krakoan layer. The strata do not blend.

## 1.7 Earliest Behavioral Patterns Carried Forward

For the file's longitudinal mapping, the following behaviors are documented *at origin* and recur identically across every subsequent decade:

1. **Geographic flight as primary stress-response.** Origin: the runaway from Caldecott. Recurrences: every team-departure across forty years.
2. **Suppression of birth-name / self-authorship of identity.** Origin: pre-Mystique. Recurrences: "Rogue" as chosen label; selective surname use; the marriage-name "LeBeau" adopted with notable readiness.
3. **Animal-mediated touch as substitute affective channel.** Origin: pre-mutation Caldecott. Recurrences: every era includes Rogue with horses, dogs, Lockheed, etc.
4. **Reading rooms quickly and accurately.** Origin: hypervigilance to paternal mood. Trained further by Mystique. Compounded by literal psyche-absorption. Operative through Quiet Council.
5. **Carrying central traumas privately rather than bringing them to attachment figures.** Origin: no parent to confess Cody to. Recurrences: the Danvers psyche concealed until breakdown; Gambit's secrets carried alone; the Magneto-touch consequences absorbed silently.
6. **Performed warmth (the *sugah*-and-flirt register) layered over restricted access.** Origin: post-Cody adaptation, possibly Mystique-coached, fully operational by the Brotherhood debut. The accent is real; the *belle* deployment of it is the prosthetic.
7. **Approach-to-threshold-then-retreat in intimate dyads.** Origin: the Cody learning trial. Recurrences: every romantic arc until the Carey-era integration permits the Gambit consummation.
8. **Gravitation toward charismatic-authoritarian figures as substitute containing-objects.** Origin: Mystique. Recurrences: Magneto, briefly Xavier, the structural acceptance of Krakoan governance.
9. **Pre-Cody fearlessness preserved as combat affect.** Origin: the muddy, climbing, animal-handling Caldecott child. Recurrences: the willingness to absorb hostile mutants knowing the psychic cost — a willingness rooted in a child who was physically unafraid before her body became a weapon.
10. **Loyalty as the highest virtue.** Origin: the inverted-pedagogy Brotherhood household, where loyalty was the operative ethical primitive. Subject retained the primitive and reattached it to a different object (the X-Men). This is the load-bearing positive trait of her adult character, and it is *Mystique's gift* — the one piece of the Brotherhood inheritance that survived translation.

---

*This concludes Chronology I. The file proceeds in Chronology II to the Brotherhood operational period (~age 14 to the Danvers absorption, Avengers Annual #10) and the immediate post-defection arrival at Xavier's, where the patterns established in this section meet their first sustained external test.*


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

*Subject: Anna Marie (legal surname variably recorded; later LeBeau). Period under review: approximately age 11 through approximately age 19 — pre-manifestation flight, mutation onset, Brotherhood recruitment, the Danvers event, and the defection. This section maps the forge.*

---

## 2.1 The Caldecott Years: Pre-Manifestation Baseline (approx. age 11–13)

**Geography.** Caldecott County, Mississippi. Backwoods bayou-adjacent terrain — cypress, kudzu, two-lane blacktop, a town small enough that a missing girl is noted at the post office before the sheriff's office. Distance to nearest interstate sufficient to make a runaway's first hitchhike a meaningful commitment. The landscape matters: subject's later spatial preferences (open ground, treelines, water at the edge of vision; aversion to crowded urban interiors except when operationally necessary) are encoded here.

**Household.** Father Owen present, mother Priscilla absent (the published record varies — vanished, deceased, "called away by the Far Banks" in the Carey retcon; what is consistent is *gone*). No siblings on record. The household is thus a single-adult-male environment with an absent maternal figure — the classic substrate for either eroticized parentification or austere distance. Evidence across decades points to the second: subject's later religious vocabulary ("Lord," "sweet Jesus," "mercy") is reflexive rather than devotional, the residue of a Protestant household where God-talk was the medium of authority rather than of consolation.

**Behavioral baseline (inferred from later patterns whose substrate must be early).** A child who is already running internal hypervigilance protocols: tracking adult mood, calibrating proximity, identifying exits. The adult subject's combat-room instinct to map cover and egress before she maps personnel is a juvenile survival skill professionalized. Her capacity to hold still for long periods (noted across decades in surveillance, infiltration, and bedside-of-the-fallen scenes) is the same skill — a child who learned that stillness reduced the probability of an adult noticing her.

**Education.** Patchy. She reads adequately and writes in a vernacular hand; she does arithmetic; she has no formal mathematics, no foreign language until the absorbed psyches gave her several. Her self-education is observational: she watches and copies. This is how she later picks up Mystique's tradecraft inside eighteen months.

**The first running.** Subject leaves the paternal house *before* mutation onset. This datum is load-bearing and routinely under-cited: she was already a runaway when she became a mutant. Whatever drove her out of Owen's house was sufficient on its own — neglect, violence, religious severity, the specific suffocations of a girl-child in an isolated rural single-father household. The published canon declines to specify; the behavior is the evidence. She does not return to that house in any decade of the record except under duress. She does not speak of her father unprompted. When pressed, her register flattens — the affective shutdown of someone whose answer is *I have decided not to think about that.*

---

## 2.2 The Mystique–Destiny Foster Period (approx. age 12–15)

**Acquisition.** Mystique and Destiny take in the runaway. The Carey-era retcons frame this as Destiny's precognition flagging the child as significant; the operational fact is that two women, one a polymorphic terrorist and one a blind clairvoyant, in an unsanctioned same-sex partnership, opened their home to a thirteen-year-old girl with nowhere to go. From the child's perspective this was, unambiguously, *rescue*. The maternal transference imprinted in those months is permanent and explains every subsequent Mystique scene across forty years of publication.

**Domestic environment.** Itinerant. Safe houses in several states; periods of stability punctuated by sudden relocations consistent with operational compromise. Subject learns to pack a bag in under ten minutes and to leave a residence without leaving traces — a skill set retained for life and visible in her adult tendency to keep her quarters under-furnished and her possessions portable.

**Affective texture of the household.** Real warmth, on the evidence. Destiny is the steadier presence — patient, didactic, a reader-aloud, the parent who explains. Mystique is the glamorous one, the parent who demonstrates and who praises performance. The child gets *attention* from both, which is more than she got from Owen, and she gets it without having to compete for it. The cost — which she will not be able to itemize until much later — is that the attention is conditional on the child's developing into a particular kind of operator. Mystique is grooming her, gently, for the Brotherhood.

**Pedagogy.** Three streams. (1) Practical tradecraft: lockpicking, surveillance detection, basic combatives, the discipline of the cover identity. (2) Ideological formation: a Magneto-aligned mutant-supremacist framing, delivered in conversational register rather than in lectures — the child absorbs the worldview the way children absorb table manners. (3) Destiny's stream: literature, history, a thicker moral vocabulary than Mystique provides, and an early introduction to the idea that the future is not a single line. The Destiny-influence is the strand that later makes subject's conscience available to be activated when the Brotherhood frame breaks.

**The two mothers as object-template.** A polymorph and a precognitive. A face that can be anyone and a gaze that has already seen everything. The structural lesson absorbed pre-verbally: *the people who love you cannot be seen straight and cannot be surprised by you.* This is the soil in which the later borderline-level identity diffusion grows. The child's developing self-concept never gets a stable mirror; it gets two mirrors that warp in opposite directions.

**Sexuality, latent.** Pre-mutation, ordinary adolescent development — interest in boys, the small social currency of being pretty in a rural school. The household's same-sex partnership is normalizing in the background; subject grows up without the homophobia she would have absorbed in Caldecott, which is a piece of moral inheritance she retains even when she discards everything else Mystique gave her.

---

## 2.3 The Cody Event: Mutation Onset (approx. age 13–14)

**The boy.** Cody Robbins. Local. By every available indication an ordinary teenage boy — not predatory, not significant, the *nearest available object* of an ordinary adolescent attraction. The triviality of his profile is part of the trauma's structure: what happened to him was disproportionate to anything about him.

**The kiss.** First kiss. Subject's first act of consensual physical intimacy with a peer. Setting: outdoor, near water in most retellings. Duration: long enough — measured later in seconds, but in the absence of any prior calibration, *any* duration was too long. The power activates without warning, without prior somatic cue, without volitional gate. Subject feels Cody's awareness flooding into her; Cody collapses.

**Immediate aftermath, observable.** The boy does not wake up. Subject runs. Whether home to Mystique and Destiny, or away into the swamp first and then home — the record is variable — she returns to her foster mothers in a state of shock with a head full of Cody's memories and skills and the somatic afterimage of his collapse. Mystique's response is operational rather than therapeutic: containment, relocation, the framing of the event as a *power* rather than as a *catastrophe*. Destiny's response is presumably more nuanced and less recorded.

**Cody's fate.** Coma. Years. He is later, in the modern record, briefly revived and lost again. For the formative period that concerns this section, the operative fact is that subject has put a person she liked into a state from which he does not return, and she has done it by trying to kiss him.

**Conditioning trial.** This is the index trauma in the strict behavioral sense. One trial, maximum salience, irreversible outcome. The conditioned stimulus class is *skin contact, especially with intimacy valence*. The conditioned response is the somatic clench, the half-step backward, the glove-check, the verbal deflection — the entire repertoire visible in every subsequent panel of her adult life. No extinction trials are possible because the unconditioned stimulus (harm to the other) is real every time. This is what makes the injury non-treatable by ordinary exposure: the feared outcome is not a phobic distortion, it is the literal physics of her body.

**Identity consequence.** The child who was already running internal hypervigilance now has a *reason*. Pre-Cody, she was wary because life had taught her to be. Post-Cody, she is wary because her body is a weapon she did not ask for and cannot disarm. The transition from environmental hypervigilance to somatic self-distrust is the hinge of her adolescent psychology, and it happens inside a single afternoon.

**Wardrobe.** Within weeks of the event, full coverage becomes standing protocol. Long sleeves, gloves, high collars, tights. The bodysuit-as-prosthetic is born here. The Brotherhood-era and X-Men-era costumes that follow are stylistic refinements of a medical countermeasure first improvised in a teenage girl's bedroom under her foster mother's instruction.

---

## 2.4 The Brotherhood Period (approx. age 15–17)

**Recruitment.** Not a discrete event — a graduation. Mystique's pedagogy was always pointed here. Subject is enrolled in the Brotherhood of Evil Mutants (later rebranded as Freedom Force) as a juvenile operative. The ideological frame is by now fully internalized: mutants are the next stage, humans are the threat, the law is the enemy's instrument, the team is the family.

**Operational role.** Force multiplier and infiltrator. Pre-Danvers, her power is itself the asset — touch a target, acquire their capabilities for a window of minutes to hours, neutralize them in the process. She is deployed against targets whose abilities are wanted and whose persons are expendable in the Brotherhood's accounting. This is moral formation by repetition: each operation rehearses the lesson that other people's bodies and minds are extractable resources.

**Behavioral pattern in this period.** Aggression front-loaded. The flirtatious-Southern-belle surface is already present in nascent form — she uses it as approach cover for targets — but the dominant register is *hard*. She fights with the abandon of someone who believes she deserves whatever comes back at her. Her later willingness to take hits, to absorb hostile mutants knowing she'll suffer the psychic blowback, is conditioned in these months: the body is contraband, expending it is permissible.

**Affective texture.** Loyalty intense and narrow. The Brotherhood is *family*; outsiders are operational categories. She does not yet have the moral vocabulary to interrogate any of this. Destiny's stream is still running underneath, providing the texts and the long-view framing, but it does not yet have purchase on her conduct.

**Social development.** Effectively arrested. No peer relationships outside the cell. No schooling. No ordinary adolescent rites — no prom, no graduation, no first job, no the-summer-I-worked-at-the-counter. She skips the entire developmental band in which most people learn that intimacy can be safely incremental, that strangers can become friends through low-stakes exposure, that a body can be in proximity to other bodies without consequence. This developmental gap is permanent. The adult subject can lead a council and command a strike team but is structurally awkward in the kinds of social environments — dinner parties, casual gatherings, civilian friendships — that her peers navigate by reflex.

---

## 2.5 The Danvers Event (*Avengers Annual* #10, fictional date concurrent with subject age ≈17)

**The operation.** Subject ambushes Carol Danvers on the Golden Gate Bridge. The published framing varies in its assignment of provocation and motive across decades of retcon, but the operational facts are stable: subject initiates skin contact, holds it past the threshold she has by now learned exists, and does not let go.

**Why she held on.** This is the question the rest of her life answers. Available factors, all of them present, none of them sufficient alone:

- *Mystique's instruction.* The operation was sanctioned and likely directed.
- *Ideological frame.* Danvers was, in the Brotherhood's accounting, an enemy combatant; the action was war.
- *The seduction of the power.* Subject had until that moment been a girl whose body was a liability. Danvers offered, through her flesh, the chance to be a girl whose body was the strongest in the room.
- *The unspoken adolescent rage* at every adult who had ever had a working body and never given hers a chance. Danvers, blonde and confident and famous and *touchable* by ordinary people, was a screen for all of it.
- *Inexperience with the irreversibility horizon.* Subject knew sustained contact could coma; she had not yet apprehended that it could also *transfer everything permanently*. She held on past the safe duration she knew, and discovered a new threshold she had not known existed.

**Immediate result.** Danvers's powers transferred permanently — flight, superhuman strength, near-invulnerability, durability. Danvers's memories, skills, language fluencies, and complete personality template transferred along with them. Danvers herself was left without powers and, more catastrophically, without the continuous thread of her own selfhood; subsequent recovery (via the Professor) restored cognition but not the affective core, which Danvers experienced as the theft of who she was. Within Carol Danvers's own subjective economy, this was a killing.

**Subject's experience in the hours after.** A teenage girl, suddenly housing the entire interior life of an adult Air Force colonel and Avenger. The Danvers psyche did not arrive as data; it arrived as a *voice*, a set of reflexes, a body-schema, a moral vocabulary, opinions about coffee and music and men. Subject's own ego — already thin from the foster-mother template and the Cody trauma — was forced to share its container with a fully-formed adversarial adult intelligence.

**Mystique's response.** Operational satisfaction. The asset is now massively upgraded. The cost — that her foster daughter is now psychiatrically compromised in a way Mystique cannot fix — is registered but subordinated to mission utility. This is the moment, in retrospect, when the maternal bond's terms become legible to the subject as terms. Mystique loves her; Mystique will also use her up.

**The Danvers persona, operational.** For the months and years immediately following, the absorbed psyche functions as an intrusive secondary identity. It surfaces under stress, under sleep deprivation, under any cue resonant with Danvers's prior life (Avengers vocabulary, military settings, a particular pitch of male voice). It argues with subject's own preferences. It pushes for tactical decisions subject would not make. It *grieves* — Danvers, inside subject's head, is grieving her stolen life, and the affect is fully transmitted. Subject is, in the technical sense, possessed.

---

## 2.6 The Hinge: Recognition and Defection (approx. age 17–18)

**Decompensation curve.** Over the months following the Danvers event, subject's functioning degrades. Sleep disturbance. Dissociative episodes — extended periods in which the Danvers persona has the controls and subject is the passenger. Loss of certainty about which thoughts, preferences, and memories are hers. The Brotherhood frame, which had been load-bearing, begins to crack: she cannot maintain mutant-supremacist conviction while housing the consciousness of a human woman she has effectively murdered.

**Destiny's stream activates.** The long pedagogy in literature, history, and moral seriousness that Destiny had been quietly conducting now has somewhere to land. Subject begins, in private, to think in categories Mystique did not teach her: *wrong*, *harm*, *unforgivable*, *redeem*. Whether Destiny precipitated the defection or merely declined to prevent it is a question the record does not settle; the precognitive's tolerance for the outcome is, however, structurally consistent with her long-game allegiances to subject herself rather than to Mystique's program.

**The decision.** Subject leaves the Brotherhood. The decision is not a renunciation of Mystique — she will return to Mystique repeatedly across decades, the maternal bond is uncuttable — but it is a renunciation of *Mystique's program*. The distinction matters and remains operative for life.

**The destination.** Xavier's mansion. This is the choice that defines her. She does not flee to a neutral place; she does not seek civilian anonymity; she does not present at a hospital. She walks toward the team most aligned with the woman she has wronged — Danvers's Avengers allies are out of reach, but the X-Men are Danvers-adjacent in moral structure, and they are the parties most likely to be able to *fix her*, and they are also the parties most likely to *hate her on sight*.

**Why this is the diagnostic move.** Most trauma-organized adolescents flee toward concealment. Subject flees toward exposure — toward the people she has most reason to fear, because she has correctly identified that her only path out of the Danvers possession runs through accountability to a community that can mirror the Danvers-shaped damage back to her and metabolize it with her. This is, in the long arc, the single healthiest decision of her formative period, and it is made by a frightened teenager with no therapeutic support and no template.

---

## 2.7 The Defection Encounter (*Uncanny X-Men* #171, subject age ≈18)

**Approach.** Unannounced. She arrives at the mansion gates without warning, without intermediary, without leverage. Wardrobe full-coverage, posture defensive-forward — the body language of someone who has rehearsed the approach and decided to ignore the rehearsals.

**Reception.** Hostile. Wolverine — whose lover Mariko she has not harmed but whose Avengers-adjacent loyalties are inflamed by Carol's status — moves to kill her on sight. Several team members second the motion in less violent registers. The mansion's standing protocol does not accommodate the surrender of an enemy combatant who is also a teenage girl in crisis.

**Storm's intervention.** Storm, then leading the team, extends provisional sanctuary. The decision is contested. Storm's reasoning — articulated in the issue and consistent with her character — is that the X-Men's mission cannot exclude the mutant who comes asking. The subordinate reasoning, which the subject reads correctly and never forgets, is that Storm has seen *the child in her* under the operator's posture and made a maternal decision the rest of the room had not yet reached.

**Subject's behavior in the immediate period.** Quiet. Watchful. Sleeps in her clothes. Eats little. Does not initiate conversation. Accepts every hostile remark without rebuttal. Performs every assigned task without complaint. This is the conduct of someone who has decided that her survival in this house depends on becoming undeniably useful before she becomes undeniably present — a pattern she retains for years and that several teammates later remark on in retrospect, having mistaken it at the time for sullenness.

**The Danvers integration arc.** Resolution of the intrusive persona requires Xavier's intervention and, ultimately, a passage through severe instability before the Danvers consciousness is psychically resettled. Subject experiences this resolution as ambivalent relief: the voice she could not silence is silenced, but the *fact of having silenced her* is one more item in the ledger of harms done to Carol Danvers. The Danvers powers — flight, strength, durability — remain in her body for years, a daily reminder. She uses them. She does not enjoy them.

---

## 2.8 Forged Structures (synthesis of the formative band)

By approximately age nineteen, the following structures are in place and will persist:

- **The somatic prosthetic.** Full coverage as standing protocol. The body as quarantined object.
- **The flirtatious-Southern surface.** Reaction-formed warmth as social interface; consciously and unconsciously deployed; the more dangerous the interpersonal moment, the thicker the accent.
- **The reparative through-line.** A life organized around the unpayable Danvers debt, sublimated into sustained pro-social labor on a team that has every reason to refuse her and that she will not allow to refuse her.
- **The disorganized attachment pattern.** Approach-flirt-escalate-sabotage-flee-return, modeled on the Mystique bond and replicated, with variations, in every subsequent primary relationship until the Carey-era integration and the LeBeau marriage partially revise it.
- **The maternal transference to Mystique.** Permanent, exploitable, unfinishable. Subject will be vulnerable to Mystique on her deathbed.
- **The Destiny inheritance.** A deeper moral vocabulary than her conduct usually displays. Surfaces under reflection, in private, in late-night conversation with the few people she trusts to hear it.
- **The Storm anchor.** First adult who held her without conditions she could detect; default referent for what a non-pathological authority looks like; the figure she models on when she herself later assumes command.
- **The two index traumas.** Cody (touch = catastrophe to the beloved) and Danvers (touch held = psychic murder). Conditioned stimulus class established; extinction unavailable because the feared outcome is physical fact, not phobic distortion.
- **The chosen contradiction.** A woman whose body cannot be touched has decided to spend her life on a team whose work is fundamentally about being in proximity to other bodies in crisis. The whole subsequent biography is the working out of that decision.

The forge closes here. The person who walks out of it — wary, courteous, dangerous, lonely, loyal past reason, gloved — is the person every later chapter will be a variation on.


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

*Operational window: from the Outback relocation (Uncanny X-Men #229, 1988) through the post–"Messiah Complex" diaspora and the closing of the second Gambit arc (circa Mike Carey's X-Men: Legacy, 2008–2010). Roughly two decades of in-universe time; the longest continuous stretch of the file. This is the period in which the patterns set down in Chronology II — the foster-mother imprint, the Cody trial, the Danvers psychic occupation, the defection — were tested, repeated, reinforced, and only partially revised. By its end, subject is recognizably the adult she will remain.*

---

## I. The Outback (Uncanny X-Men #229–251, 1988–1989): Isolation as Curriculum

The relocation to the abandoned Reavers base in the Australian interior is the first sustained environment in which subject is held inside a small, fixed, durable group with no civilian periphery to perform for. Operationally she is one of nine; in the file she registers as the team's *liminal member* — the one who cannot leave skin uncovered around even her closest colleagues, and who therefore develops the period's signature behavioral signature: the **proximity-without-contact dyad.** She begins routinely sitting *one chair removed* from whoever she is conversing with, with her own gloved hand draped across the empty seat back as a placeholder for the touch she will not initiate. This becomes a tell sustained for decades.

It is here that the **Danvers occupation acutely worsens.** The Carol persona surfaces under combat stress, takes over flight-and-strength functions during emergencies, then recedes. Subject begins keeping the bathroom mirrors in her quarters covered or angled away — first noted by Longshot in passing dialogue (#229 vicinity) and consistent with the dissociative-derealization profile in §4 of the workup. She does not want to catch her own face mid-transition and find Danvers behind the eyes. The mirror-aversion habit persists in attenuated form into the modern record: she will check a reflection deliberately, never accidentally.

**The Genosha capture (Uncanny X-Men #235–238, "Mutant Genesis"/Genoshan arc).** Captured, fitted with the inhibitor collar, subjected to the Genegineer's processing. This is the period's first datum on what subject is like *without* her power: she is, briefly, *touchable* — and she does not touch anyone. She protects Wipeout's hostages, fights free, but she does not use the inhibitor window for the obvious indulgence. Diagnostic. The deprivation has so thoroughly conditioned the inhibition that even when the medical barrier drops, the characterological one holds. The forty-eight-hour window of safe skin produces, in the published record, exactly zero attempted physical affection. She fights, she organizes, she leaves. The implication for the file: subject has internalized untouchability as identity, not merely as constraint.

**The Reavers raid and the Siege Perilous (Uncanny X-Men #246–251).** The team is shattered. Subject is overrun by Donald Pierce's reconstituted Reavers, her Danvers-borrowed durability nearly insufficient. She walks through the Siege Perilous of her own volition. This is, in the file, **the first formal index-event of suicidal-equivalence:** not suicide, but a chosen ego-dissolution offered as relief. Subject's selection of *erasure-and-rebirth* over *flight-and-return* (the option Wolverine takes elsewhere in the period) signals that by 1989 her self-concept is sufficiently aversive to her that she will take an unknown ontological risk in preference to continuing as the thing she has become. The Reverend William Stryker types of the world spend lifetimes trying to engineer what subject volunteered for in a single panel.

---

## II. The Split-Self Period (1989–1991): "Two Rogues"

The Siege returns her bifurcated. Magneto's intervention in the **Savage Land sequence (Uncanny X-Men #269, 1990)** is the formally documented psychic surgery: he forces a confrontation in which the Danvers persona and the Anna Marie persona are externalized, fight, and one is left to integrate. This is the period in which the file first records what becomes a lifelong **transferential vulnerability to Magneto.** He held her mind in his hands and gave it back; the imprint is permanent and shows up reliably across the next thirty years of operational record. Anytime subject and Magneto are in the same room, her body orientation drifts toward him — head turned three to ten degrees, weight slightly cocked — even while her verbal content is wary or hostile. This is the *containing-object* attachment described in §3 of the workup, registered somatically.

It is also in this window that the **Cajun appears (Uncanny X-Men #266, 1990).** Their meeting on the streets of Cairo, Illinois — she half-Danvers, half-herself, stranded and disoriented — establishes the template for the courtship to follow: he finds her *mid-decompensation* and is unbothered. The relational pattern is set in the first contact: he will not require her to be intact in order to be received. Every subsequent advance and retreat in their decades-long arc reverts to this baseline.

---

## III. X-Men (Volume 2) Formation and the "Blue Team" (1991–1994)

The 1991 reorganization places subject on the **Blue Team** under Cyclops. This is structurally significant: she is now under formal command-and-control rather than the Outback's improvised egalitarianism. The Blue Team period normalizes her into procedural soldiering. She runs missions, takes orders, develops a working banter rhythm with Gambit (the public flirtation that is, in private, a substitute for the contact neither can risk), and begins the long apprenticeship to leadership that will not formally pay off until Krakoa.

**Behavioral micro-patterns crystallized in this period:**

- **The "two-finger hover."** When indicating affection or reassurance, subject extends index and middle finger toward the recipient and stops them roughly two to four inches from contact, then withdraws. The gesture is recorded across dozens of issues. Functionally a substitute for the head-cup or cheek-touch she cannot perform. Recipients (Gambit, Storm, Jubilee, later Magneto and Joseph) recognize it as the maximum-permitted expression and do not flinch.
- **The glove-check.** Before any combat insertion, subject runs her right thumb across the seam of her left glove cuff, then her left thumb across her right. A double-pass equipment check that is also a *self-soothing ritual* — confirmation that the perimeter is sealed. Performed in repose as well: an anxiety tell.
- **Verbal escalation under threat.** As predicted in §5, sass increases in proportion to stress. The Southern register thickens; the "sugahs" multiply; the "darlin's" deploy as a kind of suppressing fire. When subject becomes *quiet* and accent flattens — she becomes Mississippi-plain, not bayou-confectionery — the file should treat that as a true threat indicator.
- **Flight-as-pacing.** She acquires the habit of taking to the air during arguments. Hovering ten to fifteen feet up, arms crossed, looking down at the interlocutor. Combines the Danvers gift with the avoidant defense — literally above and out of reach. Persists until power loss in the early-2000s, returns when she regains flight.

**The Magneto absorption (X-Men #25, "Fatal Attractions," 1993).** Subject contact-tackles Magneto on Avalon to prevent further harm to Wolverine; she takes in his power and his mind. She is reduced for weeks to a Magneto-puppet, speaking his cadences, contemplating his program. The file logs this as the **second formal psychic-occupation event** after Danvers, and crucially the first in which she absorbed someone she was already half-identified with. The pattern in §3 — gravitation to charismatic authoritarians as containing objects — is here literalized into her bloodstream. When the Magneto trace finally subsides she is left with a residual *familiarity* with him that she does not have to fake in subsequent encounters; she has been him.

**The Gambit absorption — "X-Men: The Wedding of Cyclops and Phoenix" prelude and X-Men #41 (1995).** A long-deferred kiss in Israel, initiated by him in the certainty he will be hurt. She receives, with the contact, his memory of the Mutant Massacre prologue — his complicity in assembling the Marauders for Sinister. She wakes; he is comatose at her feet; she runs. **This is the period's defining relational injury,** and it instantiates the pattern from §5 perfectly: approach-warmth-flirt-escalation-threshold-sabotage-flight. The sabotage was not hers, but the *flight was,* and the flight is what the file should attend to. She does not return for months. When she does, she does not raise the disclosure; she lets it sit. The two of them then maintain a *shared unmentioned trauma* as the actual ground of their bond for years. This is, by §4 standards, a textbook trauma-bonded dyad: durable, exclusive, organized around the secret.

---

## IV. The Antarctic Abandonment and Its Aftermath (1996–1998)

**Uncanny X-Men #350 (1997), "Trial of Gambit."** Subject and the team confront Gambit with the absorbed memories. Subject *leaves him in the Antarctic.* The file logs this as the **single most violent enactment of the avoidant-overlay defense** in her published record. Magnitude: she abandons her primary attachment in a polar wasteland under conditions she has reason to believe are lethal. Affect during the act: flat, accented, controlled. Affect afterward: she takes a motorcycle and rides the continental United States for months, alone, the **"Rogue: Going Rogue" road arc.** This is the period's geographic-flight beat at its most pronounced — and the file should note the specific somatic-regulation function the road serves for her. The motorcycle vibrates her body for hours at a time; engine drone substitutes for the unavailable C-tactile afferent input; the helmet is a sensory-deprivation chamber that quiets the absorbed-personality whispers. She is **self-medicating with proprioceptive load** because she cannot self-medicate with skin.

**Behavioral residue of the road period:** she keeps, thereafter, a packed go-bag in every domicile she occupies. Cash, fake ID, gloves. Verified across Westchester, San Francisco, Utopia, Krakoa-era residences. The bag's contents shift over the decades; the *practice* does not. Subject can leave any environment in under four minutes from a standing start. This is the chronic-trauma signature of someone for whom *the option to vanish* is itself a mood stabilizer.

**The brief return to romantic intimacy with Joseph (the Magneto duplicate, c. 1997–1998).** Subject permits a courtship with Joseph that she will not permit with Gambit in this window. The dynamics are §5 again: Joseph is the *clean* version of the containing-authoritarian template — the imprint without the crimes. She is, in effect, dating Magneto with the etiology removed. Joseph dies in the "Magneto War" (1999); subject grieves in muted, lateral form — she does not eulogize, she goes operational. The file should mark this as **the period's clearest demonstration that the Magneto-template attachment is a permanent fixture of her object-world,** independent of which body it currently occupies.

---

## V. The "X-Treme X-Men" Diaspora and Destiny's Diaries (2001–2004)

Storm pulls a splinter team off-campus to recover **Destiny's Diaries** — the precognitive notebooks of subject's foster co-mother. The mission is custom-built to subject's psychology and Claremont (returning to the property) knows it: she is asked to *go retrieve the words of the mother who saw through her.* The file logs the period as **the first time subject is asked to integrate her foster-family inheritance rather than flee it.** She does the work. She also, during this stretch, briefly loses her absorption power and gains a *defensive force-field* power instead (Claremont's revision). For roughly eighteen months of in-universe time she can be touched.

What she *does* with this window is the diagnostic gold of the period. She does not become promiscuous. She does not throw herself at Gambit. She experiments cautiously: hugs Storm (verified, X-Treme X-Men run), permits Bishop to grip her shoulder, accepts a hand on the arm from Sage. **The pattern is contact with same-sex peers and trusted authority first, romantic partners last.** This is consistent with the §3 reading of the relational hierarchy: the deepest fear is not contact per se but *contact that matters in the way Cody mattered and Carol mattered.* Sororal and collegial touch is rehearsed; intimate touch is approached and deferred.

When the absorption power returns (it does), the contact window closes and she does not appear to have used it for any of the indulgences a less-organized personality would have prioritized. The file should record this as **major positive evidence of ego strength** under §5's strengths-not-to-under-weight clause.

---

## VI. The "Reload" / Mike Carey Threshold and the Albany Move (2004–2007)

Subject relocates with a small team — including the **Cajun, Cannonball, Iceman, Mystique (incognito), Lady Mastermind, Karima Shapandar** — to a safe-house operation pursuing rogue mutant threats. The period is the first in which she holds **formal field command** for an extended run. The §3 prediction holds: under sustained authority, she stabilizes. Sass attenuates; procedure tightens; the glove-check ritual remains but becomes brisker.

**Mystique re-enters under deep cover.** Subject's response when the deception is exposed is the **load-bearing demonstration of the §5 pressure-point regarding the foster mother.** Subject does not kill her. Subject does not even fully banish her. The cycle — cut off, reabsorbed, cut off again — is exactly as the file predicted; this period's enactment is just the most thoroughly documented one. The intervals shorten as subject ages: by the modern record she will cut Mystique off in hours rather than years, which is growth, but she will not close the door, which is the limit of growth. The maternal transference is permanent.

**Pandemic / "Rogue Cure" attempts and the Pulse arc.** Subject contracts an absorption-overflow condition; her power begins killing those she absorbs even on brief contact. She becomes, briefly, a **strict-liability lethal weapon.** The file should note her response: she does not retreat. She *quarantines herself functionally* — extra layers, perimeter discipline — and *keeps working.* This is the reparation drive in §3 expressed under maximum operational pressure: she will not stop being useful even when being-present is hazardous to bystanders.

---

## VII. "Messiah Complex" and the Hope Arc (2007–2010)

The birth of the first post-M-Day mutant child reorganizes the entire X-Men line. Subject's role is, at first, peripheral; she becomes central in **X-Men: Legacy (Carey)** when she is selected — by circumstance, by Cable, by the logic of the story — to be one of Hope Summers's protectors and, in the Bastion-era follow-on, a mentor figure to the next generation. The selection is the universe rhyming the §3 compensatory mechanism: the woman who could not be safely held becomes the woman who safely holds others. **Mentorship of younger mutants in this period is heavy and continuous.** Subject is documented as the X-Man who will sit up with frightened students; who will fly a panicking trainee out to the desert at 3 a.m. for a low-stakes flight lesson; who will not perform the "tough love" pedagogy she was offered by Mystique and will instead offer the patient, hands-off, *fully clothed* presence that is the only kind of holding she has ever been able to give. This is the period's most important growth datum.

**The Carey-era power integration arc.** Across X-Men: Legacy subject works toward the first sustained therapeutic resolution of the absorption pathology. She learns to *channel* rather than passively receive — to call up an absorbed psyche deliberately for tactical use and then dismiss it. The mechanism in the fiction is psychic-discipline; the metaphor under the mechanism is the §3/§4 work — **integration of dissociated material into a unified ego.** The arc is partial, never total, but real. By its end she can sit in a room with absorbed voices and not be drowned by them. The file should mark this as **the period's defining therapeutic gain** and the precondition for everything in Chronology IV (the marriage, the council seat, the late authority).

**Use of the new control.** As predicted in §1 of the workup: she uses it almost exclusively to *touch teammates protectively in combat.* She does not, in this window, use it to consummate the Cajun relationship. She uses it to grab a falling Anole bare-handed mid-collapse, to slap a hand on Pixie's forehead to ground a teleport, to brace Hellion when he is overloading. The choice is diagnostic. The first applications of the rehearsed safe-touch capacity are *parental and collegial,* not romantic. The romantic application is deferred to Chronology IV.

---

## VIII. Cross-Cutting Patterns of the Middle Period

Over these two decades the file should mark the following longitudinal consolidations:

**The flirtation register becomes a public performance she can switch off.** In the Outback it was reflexive; by Legacy it is deployable. She uses it tactically with subjects of interrogation, civilian witnesses, and any opponent she wants to underestimate her. The "sugah" is a tool. Off-duty with intimates she increasingly drops it. This is one of the period's clearest growth signs: a defense converted into a capability.

**Wardrobe evolution as identity-tracking.** The full-coverage bodysuit-and-jacket-and-gloves of the Outback (perimeter maximized, body legible only as silhouette) shifts across the period toward more form-revealing variants (the green-and-yellow with the bare midsection, late 1990s) — and then *back* toward fuller coverage in the Carey era (the green-black with high collar, gauntlets). The file reads the cycle as: defended → counter-phobic display → reintegrated defense. The midsection-baring period correlates with the Joseph and pre-Antarctic Gambit window — i.e., with peak counter-phobic management of the touch fear by *displaying the body that cannot be touched.* The return to coverage correlates with the post-Antarctic, mentorship-heavy stretch in which the display function is no longer needed.

**Sleep architecture.** Repeatedly shown in panel and dialogue as poor. Subject sleeps in long gloves and long sleeves even when alone — verified across Outback, Mansion, Albany, Utopia-era panels. The medical reading: she cannot risk somnambulant contact even with herself's metaphor of safety. She is also a documented **early riser** (kitchen scenes at dawn across multiple runs) and a **light sleeper** (she wakes first to alarms in shared-quarters sequences). The pattern is hyperarousal-consistent (§4) and persists across the entire period.

**Diet.** Heavy Southern-coded comfort food when off-mission and cooking for herself or others — biscuits, gravy, fried chicken, sweet tea — the cuisine of the foster household. Civilian-fit when in cosmopolitan company. Subject *cooks* as a substitute caregiving channel: she will feed people she cannot embrace. The kitchen becomes, across the period, her preferred mansion room. File should treat the act of cooking-for as her primary non-verbal love language.

**Romantic deferrals.** Across twenty years she sustains a courtship with the Cajun that is consummated approximately *never* in genital terms (Comics-Code era notwithstanding, the panel record is consistent that physical intimacy is approached, ritualized, deferred). Joseph is the one window of actual intimacy and he dies. The period closes with the relationship reset: she and the Cajun separated geographically, he off-team, she leading. The file's prediction in §3 — sabotage at the threshold — has been demonstrated across the period in every configuration the medium permits.

**Loyalty under cost.** She does not defect from the X-Men across the entire period despite (a) Mystique's repeated recruitments, (b) Magneto's standing offer, (c) the Brotherhood and Acolytes' availability, (d) multiple opportunities to retire to the road or to Caldecott. The §5 strengths note holds across two decades: durable past reason.

**Violence profile.** Subject is, across the period, increasingly the X-Man assigned to **absorb-and-neutralize** opposing mutants — Pulse, the Children, various Acolytes, occasional A-listers. She takes the psychic-blowback hit willingly and recovers. The file should note this as a **specialized self-sacrificial role** she has volunteered into; she trades the integrity of her own ego-borders for tactical advantage on a per-mission basis. No one else on any team is asked to do this. She has built a career around being the one whose interior is breached so the team's exterior can hold.

---

## IX. State at Period's Close

By the end of the Carey run subject is: power-integrated to a working degree; field-commanding small teams effectively; mentoring the next generation with active investment; separated from the Cajun but with the relationship dormant rather than terminated; in a stabilized hostility-with-residual-attachment configuration with Mystique; carrying the absorbed psyches as resources rather than parasites; and recognizably the adult who will, in Chronology IV, sit the Quiet Council and consent to marriage.

The middle period did not heal her. It taught her to **work the wound** — to use it, to mentor through it, to lead with it visible. The §5 core drive (to be known and held without destroying) is unchanged. What changed is her competence at building everything *adjacent* to that drive into a functional life: the cooking, the mentorship, the command authority, the chosen family, the controlled flirtation, the deliberate restraint. The middle period is the long apprenticeship in adaptation. The marriage and the council seat in Chronology IV are not the resolution of the wound; they are the harvest of this apprenticeship.


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

## SUBJECT: ROGUE (Anna Marie LeBeau, née Adler per Mystique's later disclosures; legal surname inconsistent across documentation)

---

## 4.1 Entry-point to the current era: the Krakoan threshold

The bridge from the prior chronology section into the present begins with the establishment of the Krakoan nation-state (Hickman, *House of X* / *Powers of X*, 2019) and ends with the subject occupying a seat of structural authority she would not have credited herself capable of holding a decade earlier. Track the arc as a *promotion under duress*: she is offered citizenship in a polity she did not design, finds herself married inside the first year of it (*Mr. and Mrs. X*, Thompson, 2018–19, immediately preceding the Krakoan reframe), and within three publication-years is sitting on the Quiet Council (*X-Men*, Duggan, 2021– ) as the rank-and-file representative — the only Council member whose mandate is explicitly *the ordinary mutant in the street*. This is a category jump. Subject has been a field operator, a fugitive, a defector, a teammate, an off-roster wanderer; she has never before been an *institutional* person. The transition is observable in real time across the issues and shows in her body — she stands differently, sits at tables rather than leaning in doorways, listens longer before speaking. The Southern-coquette register is dialed down by perhaps a third in Council scenes; the operational register is dialed up.

The marriage to Gambit (*Mr. and Mrs. X* #1, June 2018; ceremony performed by Storm, witnessed by Kitty Pryde who is unable to walk her own aisle in the parallel ceremony — a structural irony the subject privately registers and never publicly discusses) functions as the prerequisite for everything that follows. Without the load-bearing dyad in place, the Council appointment would have destabilized her along the old geographic-flight axis. With it, she has a place to *return to* after Council days, and that return-object is the variable that finally breaks her decades-long pattern of fleeing institutional commitment after eighteen to thirty-six months.

## 4.2 The Krakoan period proper (2019–2024 publication / collapsed in-universe to roughly 18–30 months)

**Citizenship and residence.** Subject is resurrected-eligible under the Five protocols (she has not, to file date, required resurrection; the eligibility itself is a psychological datum — the *contaminated object* now has a backup). She and Gambit maintain a private residence on Krakoa rather than communal Treehouse accommodation: this is the first time in her published life she has lived in a structure that is hers. Domestic micro-observables consistent with someone unfamiliar with the form: she over-tidies guest spaces, keeps an excess of food on hand, leaves Gambit's effects undisturbed in their actual scatter (the willingness to *not* organize his side of the dwelling is itself a marker of relational security; the early-Claremont-era subject would have either fled the cohabitation or compulsively curated it).
