The double hand-wash before gloving is a contamination ritual that reads — to anyone trained — as straight obsessive-compulsive symptomatology bolted onto a real medical necessity. She does not call it that. She would resent the word.

Makeup is minimal, daily, and identical: a tinted balm, mascara, a swipe of color on the mouth. The mouth-color is interesting. The mouth is the iconic locus of her trauma (Cody Robbins, first kiss, §1); she paints it every morning. Reaction formation made literal — she *decorates* the weapon.

### Coffee and the first hour

Subject drinks coffee, black, large, hot — two mugs minimum before speaking to anyone in depth. She makes it herself; she does not accept poured coffee from a host except under formal-courtesy conditions. The kitchen approach is solo. If others are in the kitchen she will greet them with the cultivated drawl ("Mornin', sugah") and move efficiently around them, body angled to avoid passing within a forearm's length of any bare arm or neck. Surveillance footage of any communal X-residence kitchen would show her **threading**: a specific, practiced path-finding through crowded space that maintains a 14–18 inch buffer from every body. She has done this so long she does not know she is doing it. New teammates notice within a week.

She eats breakfast. Not large, not skipped — eggs, toast, fruit, whatever the kitchen has. She does not have an eating disorder; she has a body she resents but does not punish. The absence of the expected pathology here is itself a datum (§3, *compensatory mechanisms — positive*).

---

## II. WORK PATTERNS

### Training

She trains *daily* and trains *hard*. Power-set permitting, she flies — long arcs, dawn light, alone. The flight is not recreation; it is the only environment in which her body moves through space without endangering anyone. Surveillance would log it as the single most consistent behavior in her week: 40–90 minutes of solo air-time, almost every morning she has flight available, across every era she has had it. When she lost flight (the Carey integration arc; certain post-Krakoa beats), her morning ritual reorganized around long runs — same duration, same solitude, same function.

Combat training is mixed-session and *contact-oriented*: she spars in the Danger Room with teammates she trusts not to be damaged by an accidental graze (Logan with his healing factor; Colossus in armored form; Piotr generally; nobody fragile). She specifically *requests* full-contact partners. The body wants contact. The session is, among other things, the closest legal substitute for touch her physiology allows.

She runs the Danger Room solo as well — frequently, late, when others have cleared out. Solo sessions are markedly more violent than her sparring sessions. This is the controlled-release valve §3 identifies.

### Council / leadership / mission ops

On Krakoa-era days when she sits the Quiet Council, she dresses up — actual structured clothing, hair done, the Southern-belle register turned up *one click* as social armor for a hostile room. She arrives early, never late; she takes the same seat or position when she can; she reads the room before speaking; she speaks *less* than her seniority would justify and her contributions are short, concrete, and load-bearing. People who underestimate her in council learn not to twice. This is the Mystique-trained pattern reading (§3, *cognitive style*) deployed in formal politics.

Mission-day pattern: she becomes quieter, not louder. Pre-mission she will check her own gear twice and a junior teammate's gear once unbidden. She gives the brief or receives it with full attention; she does not joke during briefings (the flirtatious surface goes off-line under operational load — a tell). In-mission she is forward, aggressive, willing to take the hit that prevents a teammate taking it. Post-mission she debriefs cleanly and then *vanishes for two to four hours.* This decompression window is a fixed feature of her week. Nobody who knows her tries to find her in it.

### Mentorship

Subject mentors younger mutants consistently — has done since the Claremont era, intensifies in Carey's run, sustains through Krakoa. Mentorship sessions are scheduled, not drop-in. She prefers to mentor *girls and young women in their first decade of mutancy*, particularly those whose powers carry contact-hazard or body-hazard dimensions. She is patient with them in a way she is not patient with her peers. She tells them things she has never said in a debrief. Surveillance would log these sessions as the one place in her week where the **inner shell becomes audible to a witness**. They are her unofficial therapy, conducted from the therapist's chair.

---

## III. DOWNTIME

### The Gambit dyad

Time alone with Gambit is the gravitational center of her off-hours. The published record — particularly *Mr. and Mrs. X* and the domestic Krakoa beats — establishes a dyad of **constant low-grade physical proximity that stops short of incautious touch**. They sit close. They lean into each other through fabric. He puts his hand on her gloved hand; she leans her covered shoulder against his arm; they share a couch with their legs entangled through denim. The choreography is rehearsed by years of practice. They have a working vocabulary of *safe contact through layers* that an observer might miss as ordinary couple-behavior — it is not; every contact is mediated and every mediation is intentional.

Even with the power-control gains of the modern era, she does not casually go skin-to-skin. Bare-skin contact with Gambit is **occasion-marked** — she initiates it deliberately, in private, often after a particular kind of evening (a shared bottle of wine she barely drinks; a long conversation; a quiet) and not in the morning, not on a mission day, not when either of them is tired. This is the single most important behavioral signal in her file: *touch, when she can have it, is sacrament, not habit.* She has been deprived too long to be casual with it now.

They cook. He cooks more. She cleans. They play cards — he cheats; she catches him; this is a recurring private joke logged across writers. They read in the same room. They watch old movies (her preference: black-and-white melodrama; his: heist pictures; they alternate). They do not have many friends as a couple — the friendships are with the team, refracted through her or through him separately.

### Solitude

When not with Gambit, she takes solitude in **outdoor, weather-exposed places**. Porches. Roofs. The grounds. Open water if available. She will sit for an hour or more without an obvious task — smoking is not a habit (she tried it in the Brotherhood era; dropped it), but the posture is a smoker's posture: outside, alone, looking middle-distance. The exposure of cheek and forehead to wind is her **substitute affective-touch channel**: wind, rain, sun on the small uncovered surfaces of her face are *the only ambient skin-stimulation she gets that is not also a hazard.* Sailer et al.'s reward substrate is, in her case, partially fed by weather. This is not poetic; it is physiological.

She listens to music — older country and blues, some gospel, the occasional Stones record (a Gambit-influence acquired taste). She reads — mostly fiction, not capes-and-tights fiction; she will read a novel slowly across weeks. Surveillance would log her holding the same paperback over a fortnight, dog-eared, gloved fingers on the page.

### Telephone / correspondence

She keeps in contact with a small, fixed list: Gambit (when separated by ops), Storm (steady, decades-deep), Kitty (variable, fond), occasionally Logan (terse and warm). She does not maintain a wide social network. She does not do social media in any era; the very idea of broadcasting the face would be aversive. Mystique calls are answered, more often than she would like to admit to herself; she rarely calls Mystique first. Destiny references are reverent and rare.

---

## IV. HABITS OF PLACE AND TIME

**Place habits.** Subject habitually positions herself in rooms with the following preferences, in priority order: (1) back to a wall, (2) line of sight to the primary entrance, (3) at least 18 inches of clear floor between her chair and the nearest other body, (4) near a window or door for egress. (1) and (2) are hypervigilance; (3) is contact-management; (4) is the geographic-flight pattern (§3) pre-loaded into the seating choice. She will rearrange a chair to meet these conditions without comment.

In transit she takes the aisle if forced to a row, the back if forced to a vehicle, the rear of a stack if forced to a corridor. She walks slightly behind the people she is escorting, not ahead — she wants eyes on backs, not backs to hers. This is Mystique-training and it never came off.

**Time habits.** Punctual to operational events, *consistently early* to meetings she fears (council, anything involving Mystique, anything involving her past). She runs *late* to social events she desires (parties at the team-house, celebrations) — a small, telling avoidance: the gatherings where uncareful drunk people might touch her are the gatherings she enters once they are already organized into seated groups. She leaves early as well. The window of her presence at any social event is shorter than her warmth at it would predict.

**Clothing as standing protocol.** Long sleeves, gloves, closed neckline, full-coverage trousers or leggings: a uniform across every era and every wardrobe change. Even on a beach. Even in bed. The fabric weight changes; the coverage does not. When the published art has briefly put her in less coverage (certain 1990s plates), the in-story behavior contradicts the visual — she still does not touch anyone. Costume changes are cosmetic; the standing protocol is medical.

**The hair.** The signature white streak is uncovered, untouched, never dyed, never trimmed away. It is one of two body-features she chose for herself in adolescence (the second being her accent, retained against assimilation pressure). She runs her gloved hand through it absently when thinking. Hair-touching is *legal* on herself; it is one of the few self-soothing contact channels that does not engage the absorption hazard at the donor end, because she is donor and recipient.

---

## V. NIGHT

### Evening wind-down

Subject does not unwind into a single ritual; she layers down. Dinner (cooked, sat-down — she does not eat standing, she does not eat in front of a screen). A drink, sometimes — wine, rarely more than one glass; bourbon on hard evenings, neat, slow. The non-pattern of substance use noted in §2 holds: she does not get drunk. She has not been *drunk* in the file in any way that mattered. The body she cannot trust will not be further compromised.

A bath, on harder nights, in addition to the morning shower — heat-seeking again. She reads in the bath. The bathroom is the most private space in any home she has lived in and the one she retreats to under stress; on bad nights she will be in it for ninety minutes.

### Sleep

She sleeps gloved. She sleeps long-sleeved. She sleeps on her side, facing the door of the room when she is alone, facing Gambit when she is not. She does not sleep on her back — a hypervigilant won't-be-caught-supine pattern. She wakes once or twice in the night, almost every night, briefly. Surveillance would note small repositioning, a gloved-hand check of her own arms, a settling. Real insomnia hits her around index-trauma anniversaries — Cody's birthday is not on a public record but the calendar weeks around it produce recognizable disturbance; the Carol Danvers absorption similarly. She does not name these dates aloud. She knows them.

### Dreams

The published record references nightmares periodically — absorbed-psyche bleed-through, the Danvers voice, Mystique faces shifting. She does not discuss them. She wakes, sits up, gloves still on, breathes, lies back down. If Gambit is present and woken, the dyad has a wordless protocol: he does not ask; she does not explain; he puts his sleeved arm across her waist; they wait it out.

---

## VI. WEEKLY RHYTHMS

A full week of surveillance would compose roughly as follows:

- **Five mornings** of solo flight or run at dawn (45–90 min), invariant.
- **Five or six** Danger Room sessions (mixed sparring and solo), late morning or afternoon.
- **One to three** Quiet Council or analog leadership sessions (Krakoa era); in earlier eras, X-Men operational meetings of similar cadence.
- **Two to four** mentorship sessions with younger mutants, scheduled, mostly in the late afternoon when her own training is done.
- **Two or three** mission deployments or training-deployments in an active week; fewer in quiet weeks. Post-mission solitude window non-negotiable.
- **Most evenings**: low-grade proximity-time with Gambit. Cooking, reading, cards, music.
- **One evening per week, approximately**: time outdoors alone, weather-facing, for 60–120 minutes. This is a *near-religious* observance, not negotiable, and a reliable indicator of her psychological condition — if the outdoor-alone time drops out of the week, she is in trouble.
- **One call** to Storm or equivalent old-tie, roughly weekly, sometimes more in stress periods.
- **Sporadic, suppressed** Mystique contact — she will not initiate weekly; she will *respond* when contacted, more often than is wise.

### What a week would not show

No bars. No casual partying. No social media. No casual physical contact with anyone outside the Gambit dyad and the protective-combat-touch repertoire. No therapy appointments (she has never, in the published record, sustained formal psychotherapy — the mentoring of others is the closest she gets). No religious practice formally, though the Southern-Protestant moral substrate (§5) shows in her language and in a private habit of brief, almost involuntary grace-before-meals when she is tired enough to forget she has stopped doing it.

---

## VII. WHAT THE FILE READS, TAKEN TOGETHER

The week of a person who has built **an entire functional adult life on top of a continuous, biologically real deprivation** (Sailer et al., 2016, cited §2). The rituals are not eccentric; they are the engineered countermeasures of a person whose body is a hazard and who has decided, at every hour of every day, to keep working anyway. The flying, the weather-facing solitude, the hair, the painted mouth, the gloved hand checking her own arms in the dark — these are the daily-life signatures of the central injury translated into livable practice. The dyad with Gambit is the load-bearing relational structure (§5) made visible at sofa-and-kitchen scale. The mentorship is the reparation drive (§3) on a weekly calendar. The early-morning flight is the only hour of the day in which her body is not, to anyone, a danger.

A surveillance file that watched her for a week and concluded *she is fine* would have missed everything. A file that watched her for a year would see what she has built and how much it costs to keep building it.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*Subject: Anna Marie (legal surname variably Adler / Darkholme / LeBeau across the record; "Rogue" is operational since age ~13).*

What follows is the family map as it actually functions in subject's psychic economy — not the legal kinship chart. Subject has no biological siblings of record, no biological children, and a biological father from whom she was estranged before mutation onset. The functional family is a chosen and largely female one, assembled in flight from the original household and then re-assembled, several times, around different load-bearing figures. Each entry traces history, observable interaction pattern, the trust/safety calibration, the failure mode that recurs, and the leverage a hostile actor (or a clinician) could apply.

---

## 1. OWEN ADLER — biological father (Caldecott County, Mississippi)

**History.** The father's name appears inconsistently in the published record; what is consistent is the household's character. Caldecott County backwoods Mississippi; subject's mother (Priscilla, in some tellings) was absent — variously deceased, vanished into Cassidy/Carbonell-adjacent backstory, or simply gone — leaving the father as sole custodian of a girl-child in a rural, religiously conservative environment. Subject ran from the home in early adolescence, prior to mutation onset. This sequence — *flight before manifestation* — is the single most important datum about the original family: the home was already intolerable when the only thing wrong with subject was that she was a child in it.

**Dynamics.** Reconstructed from subject's lifelong avoidance pattern and the few flashback panels: a father who was emotionally cold, doctrinally rigid, almost certainly punitive, and incapable of providing the affective regulation a pre-adolescent girl required. There is no evidence in the record of overt sexual abuse; there is abundant evidence of *deprivation* — the kind of household where touch was withheld or punitive, affection conditional, and the child's interior life unrecognized. Subject's later reaction-formation around Southern-belle warmth is, among other things, a portrait-in-negative of what was absent at the source.

**Evolution.** None. Subject has not, in the published record, returned to the father, reconciled with him, mourned him publicly, or invoked him as a moral reference point. He is the structuring absence — the thing she ran from that made every subsequent attachment a re-trial of the original failure. The closest she comes to acknowledgement is the recurring Caldecott imagery (the swamp, the rural Mississippi cadence, the gospel registers in her speech under stress) — the *sensory* residues of the home survive in her, even though the man does not.

**Trust / safety calibration.** Zero. The father is the original proof that the strongest party in a child's life can withhold the thing the child needs most. Every later "containing authority" subject has tested (Xavier, Magneto, Mystique-as-mother) is being tested against this baseline.

**Failure mode.** Not a failure mode in the active sense — he is sealed off. The failure mode he *generated* in subject is the foundational template: *the powerful adult will not hold you; therefore you must run, and you must find your own holders, and you must doubt them when they offer to hold you.*

**Leverage.** Low direct leverage (he is functionally a ghost in her life) but high *thematic* leverage: any communication that frames her as having been *unworthy of being held* by a parent will land. Mystique exploits this register routinely. A skilled hostile interrogator invoking the Mississippi material — the church, the father's voice, the smell of the swamp — would access affect she does not access voluntarily.

---

## 2. PRISCILLA / "MAMA" — biological mother (status: absent, presumed dead in operative timelines)

**History.** Variously written as deceased in subject's early childhood, lost to Mystique-era machinations, or simply unaccounted for. The operative fact for the file is that the mother was *gone before subject was old enough to remember her as a coherent person.* This is materially different from a mother who died when subject was 12 (which would leave a mournable object) or a mother who left visibly (which would leave a grievance). What subject was left with is an *absence shaped like a mother* — a slot the psyche kept open and tried, repeatedly, to fill.

**Dynamics.** Inferential. Subject's pattern of seeking older female mentors with maternal valence — Mystique (catastrophically), Destiny (more benignly), Storm (the successful instance), eventually Carol Danvers in a perverse incorporated form — is the behavioral signature of an unfilled maternal slot. Subject does not idealize the lost mother in the record; she does not have enough data to idealize her. The absence operates as a *vacuum* rather than a *standard*.

**Evolution.** None directly. The evolution is in the *substitutes*: each successive maternal figure is chosen, tested, and either retained as anchor or discarded as failure, in a search pattern that has not terminated in the published record.

**Trust / safety calibration.** Not applicable to the mother herself. The calibration shows up as a *willingness to risk* on maternal substitutes that exceeds what a securely-mothered subject would risk — she gives candidate mothers an unusual amount of initial credit, which is precisely what made the Mystique catastrophe possible.

**Failure mode.** The vacuum draws in unsuitable applicants. Subject's pattern of attaching to maternal figures *before adequately vetting them* is a direct expression of the mother-shaped void.

**Leverage.** Anyone willing to perform the maternal role convincingly enough has a window. Mystique demonstrated this; the lesson did not generalize. A hostile actor presenting as warm, older, female, and protective will be granted access faster than subject's stated principles would predict.

---

## 3. RAVEN DARKHOLME ("MYSTIQUE") — foster mother, the central distorted attachment

**History.** Subject was taken in by Mystique sometime after her flight from Caldecott — Mystique and Destiny found her, sheltered her, and raised her into adolescence. Mystique was, in operative terms, the *active* parent: the disciplinarian, the trainer, the ideologue, the field-handler. She trained subject in combat, infiltration, and the Brotherhood's worldview, and deployed her — while subject was still a minor — into operations including the Carol Danvers ambush on the Golden Gate Bridge (*Avengers Annual* #10, 1981). Subject was, at that point, a 17-year-old being used as a weapon by her mother. This is the operative frame for understanding everything that followed.

**Dynamics.** Mystique provided what the Caldecott home had not: attention, training, purpose, and a sense that subject was *exceptional* and *needed.* She also provided what no parent should: targets, ideology, and the modeling that *the world owes you and you owe the world nothing.* The relationship was warm in its surface texture and predatory in its structure. Mystique is, by her shape-shifting nature, an *object whose face cannot be trusted* — subject grew up being mothered by someone whose physical identity was literally mutable, which is a near-perfect generator of disorganized attachment. Add Destiny's precognition (next entry) and subject was a child whose caregivers could neither be *seen* reliably nor *remain unseeing* of her — a double bind in the mirroring function.

**Evolution.** Decades of cycle. Subject defects to the X-Men in *Uncanny X-Men* #171 (1983) — first major rupture. Mystique returns repeatedly: as antagonist, as manipulator, as ostensible ally, as betrayer. Subject's response is patterned and predictable: initial wariness → gradual re-engagement → moment of apparent connection → Mystique reveals a long-running manipulation → subject is wounded, retaliates, withdraws → cycle reopens within 12–36 months publication time. The cycle has *not closed* even in the Krakoan era. Subject knows it is a cycle; subject cannot stop running the cycle, because Mystique is her mother in the relevant sense and there is no second one.

**Trust / safety calibration.** Subject's stated trust: near zero. Subject's *operational* trust: chronically higher than zero, because subject keeps answering the phone. This gap — between the stated and operational trust — is the most diagnostic single feature of the relationship. It is the gap a mother occupies in a daughter who has no other mother.

**Failure mode.** Mystique presents a frame that addresses a current unmet need (information about Destiny's predictions; protection of Nightcrawler; promise of family). Subject engages despite herself. Mystique extracts what she came for and discards the frame. Subject is left with the renewed proof that her mother is her mother — affection-shaped on the surface, instrumental underneath — and the renewed inability to fully sever. The failure mode is **the daughter cannot stop hoping.**

**Leverage.** Maximum. Mystique is the single most reliable lever in subject's psychology. Any operation involving Mystique — her endangerment, her need, her seeming reform, her invocation of Destiny — will redirect subject's attention. A hostile actor controlling Mystique's image, voice, or apparent welfare can pull subject off-mission. A clinician seeking the deepest unprocessed material in subject would start here.

---

## 4. IRENE ADLER ("DESTINY") — foster co-mother (deceased; intermittently restored)

**History.** Mystique's life partner across the better part of a century; subject's *other* mother in the household that raised her. Mutant precognitive whose diaries (the "Books of Truth") have become a recurring plot driver. Quieter presence than Mystique; the warmth-and-wisdom partner in the parental dyad. Killed in *Uncanny X-Men* #255 by a Reaver attack on the X-Men's Australian outback base — a death that occurred essentially in subject's professional vicinity, which subject has never publicly processed. Restored to life in the Krakoan resurrection protocols, which has reopened a relationship subject had decades to seal off as a grief.

**Dynamics.** Destiny was the *seeing* parent — and "seeing" here is doubled, because her power is to literally see the future. For subject as a child, this meant being raised by someone whose love was real but whose attention was always partly *elsewhere in time*, who knew outcomes the child could not know, and whose protection took the form of arrangements the child could not understand at the time. The phenomenology for the child is: *I am loved by someone who already knows what will happen to me and is not telling me.* This is not the same wound Mystique inflicted; it is its own injury — the injury of being *known in advance*, which prevents the child from feeling *discovered* by the parent. Healthy mirroring requires the parent to be *surprised* by the child; Destiny structurally cannot be.

**Evolution.** Subject's grief at Destiny's death is one of the underprocessed items in her file — she did not have leave to grieve openly because the X-Men's relationship to Mystique-and-Destiny was adversarial, and because Mystique's reaction (a multi-year revenge arc) crowded out subject's quieter loss. The Krakoan resurrection forces a reckoning subject had filed away. Current operational relationship is cautious, affectionate at moments, structured by Destiny's continuing role in Mystique's life — subject relates to Destiny *through* the Mystique relationship as often as directly.

**Trust / safety calibration.** Higher than for Mystique, materially. Destiny did not weaponize her. Destiny's failure was passive (the foresight withheld for ostensibly larger reasons) rather than active (the instrumentalization Mystique practiced). Subject's working position: Destiny meant well, was constrained by what she saw, and loved her in a way Mystique did not. This is probably accurate.

**Failure mode.** Destiny's mode is *withholding-for-your-own-good* — the future-knowledge parent who does not tell the child what is coming. When subject discovers, after the fact, that Destiny knew and did not say, the wound is the betrayal of *epistemic* trust rather than affective trust. Subject has absorbed several of these discoveries across the record.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Destiny is a softer lever than Mystique but a real one. The diaries — Destiny's posthumous text — function as a *voice from the dead parent* that subject cannot ignore; anything framed as "Destiny foresaw this for you" will be evaluated seriously even when subject would dismiss the same content from any other source.

---

## 5. KURT WAGNER ("NIGHTCRAWLER") — biological half-brother (via Mystique)

**History.** Revealed across long arcs (*X-Men: Unlimited* #4, *Uncanny X-Men* under Chuck Austen, codified across the 2000s) to be Mystique's biological son, abandoned at birth. Subject and Kurt were therefore raised by the same mother — non-overlappingly, since Kurt was given up — and discovered the kinship as adults already working as teammates. They are foster-siblings in the operative sense (shared mother, separate upbringings) and biological half-siblings only via Mystique's line.

**Dynamics.** Easy. Subject's relationship with Kurt is one of the least complicated bonds in her file — partly because Kurt's tactile-friendly Catholic-mystic warmth is exactly the register her wound recognizes as nourishing, partly because Kurt's own abandonment by Mystique gives them a shared *grievance* that does not require either to defend the mother to the other. They are the two surviving children of the same impossible woman, and they meet each other on that ground without needing to negotiate it. Kurt is one of the few teammates with whom subject will sit close, talk quietly, and remain still — the somatic markers of safety.

**Evolution.** Steady warming across decades. Kurt's deaths and resurrections have been occasions for genuine grief from subject, expressed more openly than for almost any other figure outside Gambit. He is the *sibling she got to keep* — the maternal household yielded one durable relationship, and it is this one.

**Trust / safety calibration.** High. Kurt is in the small set of figures (Storm, Kurt, Gambit, latterly Logan) whom subject treats as unconditionally trustworthy. The basis is character-evidence accumulated across decades plus the structural fact that Kurt has no leverage over her he would ever use.

**Failure mode.** Functionally none from Kurt's side. The risk in the relationship is asymmetric: subject would protect Kurt past the point of strategic sense, which means Kurt's endangerment is a vector for manipulating *her*.

**Leverage.** Threats to Kurt move subject decisively. Faith-based or fraternal appeals routed through Kurt are credited at face value. Subject would walk into a known trap for him without hedging.

---

## 6. GRAYDON CREED — biological half-brother (via Mystique), deceased

**History.** Mystique's other abandoned child, raised outside the family, became a prominent anti-mutant political figure, assassinated (originally by a time-traveling agent in *X-Factor* #130, 1996). Non-mutant, ideologically opposed to everything subject and her chosen family stand for.

**Dynamics.** Functionally nil at the personal level — subject and Graydon had little direct interaction, and what existed was adversarial. The relationship matters for the file primarily as *evidence about Mystique* and as a category marker (the *bad* sibling, the one who became what their mother's politics produced when turned inside out). Subject is, in the symbolic geometry of the Mystique family, the daughter who *escaped into* the mutant community; Kurt is the son cast out *toward* it by abandonment; Graydon is the son cast out *against* it. Subject understands the geometry without needing it articulated.

**Evolution.** None — closed by his death. Subject did not mourn.

**Trust / safety calibration.** N/A — adversarial throughout.

**Failure mode.** N/A.

**Leverage.** Indirect only. Invoking Graydon's existence is a way to remind subject of the *kind of mother* she had — useful as a destabilizer in a hostile interrogation, useless as a lever toward action.

---

## 7. CAROL DANVERS — the absorbed psyche as quasi-familial intrusion

**History.** Not a family member by any normal taxonomy — included here because for roughly a decade of in-universe time, Carol Danvers's personality template lived *inside* subject as an intrusive secondary identity, and the relationship that developed (and was finally resolved) functions in the psychic economy more like an internal-family-system member than like a defeated enemy. The Golden Gate Bridge ambush (*Avengers Annual* #10, 1981) imprinted Danvers's full memory set, personality, and powers into subject. The Danvers persona surfaced under stress for years, culminating in the Genoshan/Savage Land episodes where it temporarily took over (*Uncanny X-Men* #269), resolved via Magneto's psychic intervention.

**Dynamics.** Internal. Subject had to *cohabit* with a stolen consciousness — to know Danvers's mother, Danvers's lovers, Danvers's training, Danvers's politics, from the inside, while being neither Danvers nor free of her. The relationship that formed inside subject's head was not friendly: Danvers's psyche hated subject correctly and continuously. Subject's only available stance was guilt management — she could not apologize to a psyche that was *also her own intrusive thought.* This is the architecture of the central guilt of subject's life.

**Evolution.** The Danvers psyche was extracted; the *guilt* was not. Subject's external relationship with the restored Carol Danvers has been correct, distant, and unresolved across the modern era. They are not friends; they are not enemies; they are two women who share an injury whose moral weight neither has fully discharged.

**Trust / safety calibration.** The external Carol: low-to-moderate, never warm. The *internal* Carol, while she was present: an ongoing internal adversary subject learned to live with the way a chronic-pain patient learns to live with pain.

**Failure mode.** Any cue that re-activates the Danvers material (the powers themselves, when subject had them; auditory cues; visual reminders of the bridge) destabilizes subject. The wound is uncauterized.

**Leverage.** Very high in the narrow domain. Any approach that frames subject as *the woman who did that to Carol Danvers* will produce the largest reaction in her behavioral repertoire. Mystique knows this and has used it. A hostile interrogator would use it within the first hour.

---

## 8. CODY ROBBINS — the first boy; comatose for years

**History.** A boy from subject's adolescent Mississippi life; her first kiss; the first triggering event of her mutation. Cody fell into a coma from the contact and remained there for years (depicted across flashbacks throughout the 1980s–1990s; eventually died after extended unconsciousness). He was, in every functional sense, the first person subject ever loved romantically, and the proof that she could not.

**Dynamics.** No dynamics post-incident — he was unconscious. The relationship that persists is *with the memory of him* and with the moral fact of what happened to him. He functions in subject's psychology as the *first victim*, the case before Danvers, the original demonstration that intimacy from her hand is a weapon. Every romantic threshold subject has approached since age 13 has been evaluated against the Cody precedent.

**Evolution.** Subject has revisited the Cody material in flashback and in a small number of explicit on-page reckonings; she has never fully metabolized it. The Cody figure remains a private chapel in her interior architecture — visited rarely, kept in order, never demolished.

**Trust / safety calibration.** N/A — the relationship is with a memory.

**Failure mode.** Any new intimacy reactivates the Cody template. The reactivation is preconscious — she does not choose to think of him; the thought arrives at the threshold.

**Leverage.** A skilled hostile knowing the Cody material can use it to disable any approach toward romantic or tactile vulnerability. Subject's defenses against this material are mature but not absolute.

---

## 9. THE FOSTER HOUSEHOLD AS A SYSTEM — Mystique/Destiny as parental unit

A separate note, because the dyad operates as a *system* distinct from either member individually. Mystique and Destiny together constituted a *lesbian foster household* in the Deep South / wandering-outlaw context — a structurally non-normative family that gave subject one of the few unambiguous *gifts* of her origin: the lived knowledge that family is constructed, that women can love women durably, and that legitimacy is not the same as legality. Subject's later capacity to assemble chosen families (the X-Men, the Gambit marriage, mentorship of younger mutants) draws on this template, which is the *good* inheritance from Mystique and Destiny even as the rest of the inheritance is toxic. She has not, on the record, articulated this gratitude — it is structural, not stated. A complete file notes both halves of the ledger.

---

## 10. THE ABSENCE OF CHILDREN

Subject has no biological children. The reasons are overdetermined: the power foreclosed the conception event for most of her life; the trauma history foreclosed the desire for most of her life; the operational tempo of X-Men service foreclosed the practical possibility. The post-Gambit-marriage era has raised the question in the published record without resolving it. For the file, the *absence* is itself a datum: subject has redirected the generative drive into mentorship (younger X-Men, particularly female ones; the Krakoan training contexts) and into the Council-level governance role. The maternal capacity she did not receive she has constructed *outward* rather than reproduced *downward.* If she ever does have a child, the file predicts: extreme protective vigilance; high risk of repeating the Mystique-pattern of over-control; compensating awareness of that risk; probable success, because subject's capacity for hard self-correction is one of her better-attested traits.

---

*End Section. Continues: Relationships II — Chosen Family, Lovers, and the X-Men.*


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*Dossier Section 7B. Subject: Anna Marie LeBeau (ROGUE). Scope: non-romantic, non-adversarial relational matrix. Romantic partners and antagonists filed separately (sections 7A, 7C). Mystique and Destiny filed under 7D, Foster-Maternal, owing to the formal foster-parent designation and the unresolvable transferential weight.*

---

## 1. ORORO MUNROE (STORM)

**Origin of the bond.** *Uncanny X-Men* #171. Subject walks into the Xavier mansion uninvited, carrying the Carol Danvers psyche as a passenger, with Mystique's stink still on her, asking for help. Wolverine puts claws to her throat; Storm — then in her mohawk-era authority phase — *overrules him.* That moment is the foundational datum of the relationship and one of the foundational data of subject's adult life. Storm did not embrace her; Storm *adjudicated for her,* extending the institutional shelter of the team over an applicant the team had every reason to reject. Subject correctly read the act as moral seriousness rather than warmth, and this is the form of care she trusts.

**Dynamic.** Older-sister/commanding-officer hybrid, weighted toward the command vector. Storm does not coddle. Storm makes room. Subject, who was raised by a shapeshifter and a precognitive, has spent her entire life waiting to be seen-through, played, or rewritten; Storm is the first adult in her file who *takes her at face value* and then *holds her to it.* Subject responds with a fierce, almost feudal loyalty that has not wavered in forty in-universe years. On panel she is one of the few people permitted to use the diminutive of Storm's name without rebuke; off the operational frame she defers to Storm's judgment in disputes she would contest with anyone else, including Xavier.

**Evolution.** Phase one (1983–1990): subject as Storm's project, watched, occasionally hugged through fabric, given missions calibrated to rebuild competence and earn team trust. Phase two (Outback/Australia era): peer combat operators, Storm de-powered for stretches, the deference relaxes into something like sisterhood-in-arms. Phase three (1990s into 2000s): parallel command tracks; Storm in and out of Wakanda, subject in and out of the field-team leadership; their reunions are short, dense, immediately operational. Phase four (Krakoa, Council era): institutional peers. Subject sits on the Quiet Council partly because Storm's pattern of authority-via-restraint became the model she internalized.

**Trust / safety.** As high as the subject is capable of registering with a non-romantic other. Storm is one of the three people (Gambit, Kurt, Storm) in whose presence the file documents subject *removing her gloves with intent and without panic* — and with Storm the intent has never been to make contact but to demonstrate trust by exposing the apparatus of her own dangerousness. The gloves come off in the room; the hands do not extend. That distinction is the entire relationship.

**Failure mode.** Subject's loyalty to Storm can override subject's own judgment. If Storm asks, subject goes — even on a mission subject would otherwise refuse. The corollary risk: if Storm were ever to be impersonated (Mystique-tier shapeshift, Skrull substitution, telepathic override) subject's compliance window would be longer than her usual paranoia warrants. The substitution attack vector is real and underexploited by adversaries.

**Leverage (use with care).** Storm cannot be weaponized against subject directly — the bond is too clean — but Storm can be used to *route* subject. A request relayed through Storm receives a different threshold of consideration than one received cold. Conversely, threat-to-Storm produces immediate, disproportionate mobilization in subject; she will travel continents.

---

## 2. KURT WAGNER (NIGHTCRAWLER)

**Origin and structural irony.** Subject is the foster daughter of the woman who *abandoned* Kurt as an infant. The genealogical fact (Mystique → Kurt; Mystique → Rogue as foster) makes subject and Kurt step-siblings in the only sense Mystique permits her own kinships to be tracked. They arrived at this knowledge in stages over decades of publication. The remarkable datum: it did not poison the bond. Kurt, characterologically incapable of holding inherited debts against a person, absorbed the revelation; subject, characterologically *expecting* to be hated for adjacencies to Mystique, was undone by his refusal to hate her.

**Dynamic.** Quietly the safest male friendship in subject's file. Kurt's signature mode — courtly, German-inflected formal warmth, theological seriousness under swashbuckler surface — happens to be the exact register subject's reaction-formation defenses are built to *receive without triggering.* He flirts in a way that is unmistakably non-predatory; she flirts back without the escalation tax that her flirtations with almost everyone else accrue. Their conversations in the record are disproportionately about *sin, redemption, mothers,* and *the body* — the four topics on which she is least able to speak with anyone else.

**Evolution.** Early period (mid-1980s): Kurt is wary of her as a former Brotherhood operative; the wariness erodes over shared missions. Middle period: they discover the Mystique link; both recoil; both metabolize it. Late Claremont and 1990s: she will tease his collar; he will offer to teleport her out of any room she signals she wants to leave. Modern era: he is one of the few teammates who has, in print, *physically embraced her through her uniform with full body contact* without either of them flinching — a level of intra-team intimacy she does not extend to most.

**Trust / safety.** Maximal in the non-romantic register. Kurt is the priest-figure in her life, even when he is not formally ordained — she will tell him things she will not tell Storm because Storm will *act* and Kurt will only *witness.*

**Failure mode.** If Kurt invokes his faith to ask her for something, she will agree past her own threshold. She converted, structurally, to his framework on questions of soul and forgiveness during the long aftermath of the Danvers reparation arc, and she still defers to him on theological matters her own Mississippi-Protestant substrate cannot fully resolve.

**Leverage.** Kurt's safety, like Gambit's, is a hard pressure point. Threats to Kurt produce mobilization without negotiation. More subtly: a counterfeit message *in Kurt's diction* would penetrate her filters faster than a similar message in any other teammate's voice, because his cadence is one she does not interrogate.

---

## 3. LOGAN (WOLVERINE)

**The death-threat origin.** First meeting (*UXM* #171), Wolverine is the one who puts steel near her windpipe and tells the room he will kill her if she breaks faith. Subject — and this is the diagnostic move — *agreed with him.* She did not flinch from the threat; she filed it as legitimate. This is the only viable starting point for a relationship with Logan, and she found it intuitively.

**Dynamic.** Older-feral-uncle. Bluntness as the medium of affection. Subject and Logan share the structural fact of having a body that *does things to other people whether they wish it or not* (his claws; her skin), and this shared somatic condition is the unspoken substrate of every interaction between them across forty years. Neither has to explain to the other why armor is not optional.

**Evolution.** Phase one: probation, monitored. Phase two (Outback/Madripoor stretches): drinking-buddy register, except she does not drink, so it is iced-tea-and-bourbon on adjacent stools while he watches a door. He is one of the very few people the file shows her in extended unsupervised proximity to without escalation in either direction. Phase three: she takes hits for him in the field; he takes hits for her; the ledger is never spoken aloud. Phase four (post-resurrection Krakoan): an old-soldier register, the two of them the institutional memory in rooms full of younger operators.

**Trust / safety.** High but narrow. She trusts Logan with her life and with her perimeter; she does not trust him with her *interior* (she takes that to Kurt and to Storm). Logan, for his part, has been documented permitting her to absorb him in extremis — knowing she will get his healing factor for a window and his memories permanently. This is, in his economy, the most intimate gift available; subject understands this and has only ever accepted it under operational necessity.

**Failure mode.** If Logan goes feral or is mind-controlled (recurring problem), subject's first instinct is to *close the distance* — she is one of the few people who can shut him down via absorption. She has done this and accepted the psychic load. The risk: each such absorption deposits more of Logan's memory set into her, including the parts of his history that are themselves trauma payload.

**Leverage.** Logan cannot be used against her directly; he can be used to *escalate* her — if Logan is endangered, she moves without waiting for sanction.

---

## 4. REMY LeBEAU (GAMBIT)

*Filed in detail under 7A, Primary Romantic. Cross-referenced here because pre-marriage the relationship operated for years as ally/chosen-family rather than as consummated partnership, and the chosen-family registers persist inside the marriage.*

**Allied-register summary.** Before the courtship resolved, Gambit was the teammate she could spar with at full verbal speed, the only person in the building whose secrets matched hers in *quantity* if not in *kind,* and the running partner she trusted at her back in a Madripoor alley. The romance grew out of an alliance, and when the romance is under stress the alliance is the load-bearing layer that holds. The marriage did not displace the partnership; it sits on top of it.

---

## 5. CHARLES XAVIER

**Dynamic.** The hardest entry to write cleanly, because subject's relationship with Xavier is *role-relationship* more than person-relationship. He is the institution that took her in when no other institution would; he is also a telepath whose entry into her head she has to authorize and re-authorize repeatedly; he is the only adult who can credibly offer her psychic intervention when the absorbed-personality intrusions break containment, and he has done so at least three times in the published record.

**Evolution.** Early: gratitude shading into deference, complicated by the fact that he initially distrusted her as much as Wolverine did and was more polite about it. Middle: working alliance, the Danvers psyche treated as a chronic medical problem he could only intermittently address. Late: subject's discovery, across the Krakoan era, that Xavier is *not* the unimpeachable moral authority she had partially needed him to be. The disillusionment did not break her — she had been raised by Mystique; her threshold for caregiver-disappointment is functionally infinite — but it relocated him from anchor to colleague.

**Trust / safety.** Conditional. She permits him in her head because she has to; she does not relax there. The Carey-era integration arc, in which power-control was finally achieved, did *not* run through Xavier — it ran through Mystique-and-self — and this is significant. Xavier helped manage symptoms; he did not produce the cure.

**Failure mode.** Subject's default of deference to institutional authority can be exploited via Xavier's chair-and-voice. She has been moved by Xavier into actions she later regretted; the regret did not retroactively recalibrate the deference, which remains operative.

**Leverage.** A Xavier directive carries weight she will *contest* but rarely *refuse.* An apparent-Xavier directive (telepathic forgery, illusion-cast, Shadow King vector) is therefore a high-priority spoofing risk against her decision loop.

---

## 6. MAGNETO (as mentor / containing object, not as briefly-attempted romance)

**Dynamic.** The most theoretically dangerous entry in this section and the one she has navigated most surprisingly well. Magneto, during his Xavier-substitute period at the school and again during the Genoshan and Krakoan eras, became one of the charismatic-authoritarian figures her template predicts she would gravitate toward. She did gravitate. He intervened to extract the Danvers persona during the Savage Land period (*Uncanny X-Men* #269) — an act of psychic surgery that, by any honest reading, *saved her interior life.* This is a debt she has never pretended she does not owe.

**Evolution.** Phase one: mentor-of-last-resort, mediated by Xavier's absence. Phase two: brief romantic-adjacent dalliance, never consummated in any way her power would permit, terminated when his pathology re-asserted (*Fatal Attractions,* in which her absorption of him produced the psychotic episode). Phase three: long, careful distance. Phase four (Krakoan): peer on the Council, the past explicitly bracketed, his authority acknowledged and his judgment audited.

**Trust / safety.** Low and *operationally calibrated.* She trusts his commitment to mutant survival; she does not trust his judgment about individual mutant lives, hers included. She does not turn her back on him in a room, though she would never say this.

**Failure mode.** The gratitude for the Savage Land psychic extraction is real and persistent. If Magneto invokes that debt, the call will reach her. He has not invoked it. He may.

**Leverage.** As a vector against her: medium-high in crisis, low in steady state. He is one of two people in the file (the other being Mystique) who has proven capable of inducing her to act against her current values, and he has done so without speaking, simply by being credibly endangered or credibly correct.

---

## 7. CAROL DANVERS

**The relationship that should not exist.** Subject *psychically murdered* Carol Danvers as a teenager and wore Danvers's powers, personality, and memories for two decades of publication time. By any normal reckoning this is an unrecoverable wrong. The remarkable datum is that across the long record there has been a slow, partial, ongoing rapprochement — never friendship, but something more functional than enmity.

**Dynamic.** Asymmetric and stylized. Danvers cannot forget, will not forgive in the warm sense, but has — across multiple writers and eras — accepted joint mission assignment with subject, declined to escalate when subject was vulnerable, and on at least one occasion saved her life. Subject, for her part, does not flinch from Danvers's presence and does not over-apologize; she has learned that excess contrition reads to Danvers as further imposition. The interactions are clipped, professional, and *attended* on both sides.

**Evolution.** Phase one (1981–early 2000s): pure unresolved trauma on both ends, brief eruptions when forced into proximity. Phase two: the Danvers psyche is finally extracted from subject; the original injury becomes, paradoxically, more discussable now that it is no longer ongoing. Phase three (modern): co-belligerents in multiple Avengers/X-Men crossovers, capable of working a tactical problem together without affective spillover.

**Trust / safety.** Operational only. Neither will harm the other; neither will confide in the other.

**Failure mode.** Anything that places subject and Danvers in a situation requiring *physical contact* between them is a high-stakes scenario; both have learned to engineer around it, but the avoidance is itself a tell. Adversaries who force the contact (illusion-cast, terrain trap) will trigger reactions in both that exceed the tactical situation.

**Leverage.** Danvers is, after Mystique, the most efficient *guilt-vector* available against subject. Any framing that re-opens the Brooklyn Bridge act will degrade subject's decision quality for the duration of the framing.

---

## 8. JEAN GREY

**Dynamic.** Sisterly, with a careful telepathic etiquette laid over it. Jean is one of the very few people in the file qualified to *understand the inside of subject's head from the inside,* and Jean has always handled this with the courtesy of a guest who waits to be invited. Subject reciprocates with a candor she does not extend to most.

**Evolution.** Slow start (Jean was dead or Phoenix during much of subject's early tenure), warming in the 2000s, settled into chosen-sisterhood in the modern era. The Jean Grey School period codified Jean (and Kitty, and Storm) as an internal women's bench subject could rely on for non-operational counsel.

**Trust / safety.** High. Jean is the telepath she would *choose* over Xavier and over Emma if a psychic intervention were ever again required.

**Failure mode.** None active. Jean's Phoenix-state instability is a latent risk to the relationship, not currently triggered.

**Leverage.** Low. The bond is durable and the channel is psychically clean.

---

## 9. KITTY PRYDE (KATE PRYDE / SHADOWKAT)

**Dynamic.** Younger-sister-as-equal, the rare friendship in which the age gap is acknowledged but not used. Kitty is one of the few teammates whose phasing power renders her *categorically safe* from subject's touch — she can simply intangible-out of any incidental contact — and this physical fact relaxes a layer of subject's vigilance she does not get to relax around almost anyone else.

**Evolution.** Built across the long Claremont run, deepened in the post-Schism and Krakoan eras when Kitty's authority track caught up to subject's. Mutual recognition of two operators who have each spent their lives running through institutions and emerging more institutional, not less.

**Trust / safety.** High. Kitty is one of the small number of people subject will tell when she is leaving and where she is going.

**Failure mode.** If Kitty asks subject to violate Council protocol for personal reasons, subject will at minimum consider it.

**Leverage.** Low and well-defended.

---

## 10. THE ORIGINAL/MIDDLE COHORT — Hank McCoy, Bobby Drake, Warren Worthington

**Dynamic, collective.** Background family in the literal sibling sense — not close confidants, but the people whose presence in a room subject does not have to assess. Hank she trusts medically; Bobby she banters with in the safe register of two operators who have agreed the flirting is purely formal; Warren she keeps at the polite distance his class background and his Apocalypse-era instability both warrant.

**Trust / safety.** Default-high through institutional accretion. None of the three is a confidant; all three are, in the technical sense, *family.*

**Failure mode.** Hank's heel-turns across recent eras have damaged the trust; subject is now in an audit posture with him she was not previously.

**Leverage.** Diffuse. None is a primary vector.

---

## 11. THE NEXT GENERATION — Mentees and Protégés

**Pattern.** Subject has, across decades, taken on mentoring roles for a series of younger mutant women — most consistently within the New X-Men and the post-Schism Jean Grey School cohorts. The pattern is diagnostic: she is producing, deliberately, the secure-attachment caregiver figure she did not receive. Storm modeled it for her; she models it forward.

**Style.** Practical, hands-off (literally and figuratively), high on direct verbal reinforcement, low on hugging. She will eat lunch with a student. She will sit on the floor of a dorm room. She will tell a fifteen-year-old that her power is not her enemy, in the exact words she needed and did not get at fifteen. She will *not* embrace the student. The students, with rare exceptions, learn to read the structure and find it more rather than less safe.

**Specific cases of note in the file.** Several New X-Men students under her care during the Decimation and post-M-Day periods received from her the explicit, on-page message that *powers that hurt people do not make the bearer a person who hurts people.* This is the central thesis of her own life, delivered to children who needed it. The labor is reparative for her, formative for them, and visible to any observer paying attention.

**Failure mode.** She over-identifies with students whose powers carry the same touch-deprivation structure as hers. She has, at least implicitly, made unwise tactical choices to spare such students experiences she herself endured.

**Leverage.** A threat to one of her students will mobilize her at the same threshold as a threat to Gambit. Adversaries who have noticed this have exploited it; most have not noticed.

---

## 12. THE QUIET COUNCIL PEERS (Krakoan era, institutional)

**Dynamic.** Not friendships. *Working colleagues* in a governing body, several of whom (Mystique, Sebastian Shaw, Exodus, Sinister at various removes) are people she would have killed or been killed by in earlier eras. Her seat on the Council is itself a personality datum — she chose institutional responsibility over the outlaw posture Mystique modeled and over the lone-operator posture Logan modeled.

**Style on the Council.** She speaks rarely, votes deliberately, reads the room with the trained-by-Mystique-and-by-decades-of-absorbed-minds accuracy that is her cognitive edge. She is the Council member least likely to be flattered, intimidated, or fooled by rhetoric. Storm's mentorship shows in her bearing; her own hard-earned authority shows in her willingness to dissent.

**Trust / safety.** None extended to the Council as a body. Specific trust extended to Storm, Kurt (when present), and — operationally and grudgingly — to a few others on issue-by-issue basis.

**Failure mode.** Mystique on the Council is a permanent destabilization vector; see §7D.

**Leverage.** Institutional capture of subject via the Council is harder than it looks. She values the *seat* more than she values the *body's approval,* and she will dissent and absorb cost.

---

## 13. SUMMARY TOPOLOGY OF THE ALLY MATRIX

Subject's chosen-family network resolves, on inspection, into a layered structure with a small inner ring and a much larger institutional periphery:

- **Innermost (3):** Gambit (romantic, filed separately), Storm, Kurt. These three have full *interior* access; with each, the gloves come off in the room as a non-verbal sign of trust, without the hands extending.
- **Inner working ring (4–5):** Logan, Jean, Kitty, sometimes Xavier, sometimes Magneto (audited). Operational confidence high, interior access limited.
- **Family-by-institution (the original/middle cohort, the broader X-roster):** background trust, accreted by time and shared loss.
- **Mentees:** the deliberately constructed downstream layer, in which subject is the caregiver she lacked.
- **Council peers:** working colleagues, not family, with Storm and Kurt as the bridges back to the inner ring.

The topology's most striking feature: it is *durable.* Subject's primary attachments persist across forty in-universe years, multiple deaths and resurrections, ideological splits, and the full Krakoan reorganization. For someone whose foundational trauma is the destruction of intimacy by contact, the size and stability of this network is, by any clinical reading, an unusually successful adaptation — and the strongest single piece of evidence that the wound, while real, has not won.


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*A taxonomy that, in subject's case, blurs at every boundary. Her enemies have been her mothers; her lovers have begun as marks; her rivals have shared her body. The categories here are operational, not clean.*

---

## I. INTIMATES & LOVERS

### Remy LeBeau ("Gambit") — Husband; Load-Bearing Relational Structure

**History.** Met in *Uncanny X-Men* #266 (1990), Cairo, Egypt — she encounters him as a de-aged, amnesiac Storm's accomplice; the meet-cute is mutual reconnaissance disguised as banter. Recruited concurrently to the X-Men. Three decades of approach-avoidance follows: courtship through *X-Men* (vol. 2) #1–24; the kiss-and-coma episode (*Uncanny X-Men* #320s era); the Antarctic abandonment (*X-Men* #45, 1995, the "Trial of Gambit" — she walks out of the snow after learning his Marauder-guide past via forced absorption); reconciliation and separation cycles through Lobdell, Nicieza, Casey, Claremont's return, Carey; cohabitation under the Carey-era power-control arc; the formal wedding in *X-Men Gold* #30 (2018) — actually subject's wedding, Kitty Pryde having balked at the altar — followed by the *Mr. and Mrs. X* honeymoon series. Krakoa-era they share a quiet residence at the Greymalkin Industries house.

**Dynamics.** The structurally healthiest relationship of her life because it was built on the exact obstacles that broke every other one. He is the only intimate who *does not require* her to solve her power as the price of presence. Both are thieves of a sort — he literal, she involuntary — and the shared knowledge that each has done something unforgivable before the other arrived produces a parity that romantic love rarely achieves. Their banter (the "Remy"/"Cher"/"sugah" register) is not flirtation in the ordinary sense; it is a *protocol* — a constant verbal touch that substitutes for the physical one they cannot have on demand. When she finally can touch him without consequence, the protocol persists. Telling.

**Trust / safety.** Trust is total in the operational sense (she will hand him her back in a firefight without looking) and *negotiated* in the intimate sense (each has, at minimum, withheld a major piece of identity from the other for years — his Marauder history; her absorbed Danvers material; her Mystique entanglements). The marriage works because both have stopped expecting clean disclosure and started expecting eventual disclosure.

**Failure mode.** He gambles, drinks, vanishes for solo jobs, keeps Louisiana commitments she is not party to; she withdraws geographically when overwhelmed and has, historically, walked out of the relationship rather than have a hard conversation. Either of them can disappear; neither has the *abandonment-resistance* most marriages assume. When they fail, they fail by *flight,* not fight.

**Leverage.** He is the single largest behavioral lever on subject in the current era. Threats to him produce decision-making that bypasses the Quiet Council seat, the moral framework, and most prior commitments. An adversary who understood this would not need her power-set neutralized — only him in a room.

---

### Magneto (Erik Lehnsherr) — Two Distinct Entanglements, Both Diagnostic

**History.** Phase one: the Savage Land sequence (*Uncanny X-Men* #274–278, 1991) — stranded together, subject de-aged in body and reset to baseline power-state, Magneto functioning as protector and (per subtext that the Claremont era pushed as far as the Code allowed) potential lover. Phase two: "Fatal Attractions" (*X-Men* #25, 1993) — she touches him to save Gambit, absorbs his power and his psyche, walks around with Magneto-in-her-head for issues afterward, an experience that combines violation, infatuation, and disgust in a ratio she has never publicly disentangled.

**Dynamics.** He is the *charismatic-authoritarian-container* archetype that her attachment system gravitates toward whenever Mystique is not occupying the role. He offered, in the Savage Land, the one thing she had never been offered: presence without sexual threat, because he chose restraint. The absorption later collapsed the distance permanently and badly.

**Trust / safety.** Operationally, she trusts him on Krakoa within the Council frame — she will vote with him on questions of mutant survival. Personally, she keeps a fixed distance; the absorbed-psyche residue makes proximity uncomfortable in a way she does not advertise.

**Failure mode.** If he asked, in the right register, she would find herself agreeing to things her conscious moral framework would reject. She knows this and routes around it by limiting one-on-one contact.

**Leverage.** Magneto knows the inside of her head literally; she knows the inside of his. Neither uses it. The mutual non-use is itself the structure.

---

### Joseph — The Cleanest Romance That Was Never Real

**History.** Mid-1990s (*X-Men* vol. 2 #46 onward). Amnesiac, biologically-younger Magneto clone/regression presented as a blank slate; subject pursued the relationship Magneto-the-elder had foreclosed. He died saving Earth from the original (*Magneto* #4, 1997).

**Dynamics.** Brief, intense, structured as fantasy: a Magneto without the history, in a body she could risk touching the gloves of. The relationship functioned as wish-fulfillment and as a controlled experiment in whether she could love an unbroken object. She could; he died; the data point did not generalize.

**Failure mode / residue.** Loss confirmed her working theory that she ruins what she loves. Joseph's death was not her fault by any reasonable accounting; she accounted unreasonably.

---

### Cody Robbins — The Index Trauma in Human Form

**History.** First kiss, Mississippi, approximately age thirteen. He went into a coma that lasted years; he died eventually off-page, with subject visiting once or twice across her adult life (*X-Men Unlimited* #4 flashback and subsequent revisits).

**Dynamics.** Not a relationship in any post-event sense — it is a *conditioning trial* that defined the entire stimulus class of "intimate touch" thereafter. Every glove she has worn for the rest of her life has Cody's name written on the inside.

**Trust / safety / leverage.** None operative; he is a ghost. But any reference to him produces immediate affective disorganization in subject — observation across multiple writers. Mentioning Cody is, in interrogation terms, a confirmed access route to her core wound.

---

### Magneto-adjacent and minor entanglements

- **Colossus** — *brief* mutual interest during the early X-Treme/Australian period flickers; never consummated; she registered him as too gentle to risk and too committed elsewhere. Functional baseline: warm, fraternal.
- **Bobby Drake (Iceman)** — close friendship with romantic edge in the Jim Lee/Lobdell era; physiology aligned (he could ice-skin to allow safe contact), but the chemistry did not escalate. He became something rarer: a male friend who registered her as a person before a problem.
- **Magneto's various adjuncts (Erik the Red bit-players, Pyro on his deathbed)** — Pyro's terminal sequence in the *Cable* run, where he asks her to absorb him so he does not die alone, is one of the cleanest emotional transactions of her life and a template for the *consensual-absorption-as-mercy* idea she has used twice since.

---

## II. RIVALS

### Carol Danvers (Ms. Marvel / Captain Marvel) — The Permanent Asymmetry

**History.** *Avengers Annual* #10 (1981) — subject, teenaged Brotherhood operative, ambushes Danvers on the Golden Gate Bridge under Mystique's direction, holds skin contact past the point of reversibility, leaves her depowered and psychically gutted. The Danvers psyche then persists inside subject for roughly a decade of publication time. Subject and Danvers have intermittently coexisted as colleagues across crossovers ever since; the relationship has never been clean and will not be.

**Dynamics.** Not rivalry in the conventional sense — it is *debt that cannot be repaid.* Danvers has, at various points, attempted forgiveness, attempted vengeance, and attempted ignoring; none has resolved. Subject cannot face her without somatic guilt; Danvers cannot face her without somatic violation. They are linked by the worst single act of subject's life.

**Trust / safety.** Zero baseline trust on Danvers's side, earned and proper. Subject trusts Danvers in the narrow sense that she expects Danvers to behave morally — including, perhaps, to one day decide reckoning is overdue.

**Failure mode.** Any sustained co-deployment risks Danvers's containment of her own (legitimate) rage failing. Subject's containment of her own guilt then fails in sympathy. Outcome: tactical collapse plus interpersonal disaster.

**Leverage.** *The* defining lever on subject. Anyone who can credibly threaten to reopen the Danvers question — legally, narratively, telepathically — owns subject for the duration of the threat.

---

### Mystique (Raven Darkhölme) — Foster Mother / Eternal Adversary / Most Dangerous Person Alive To Her

*Treated in depth in the Family section; relisted here because she is also, structurally, subject's most consequential enemy.*

**Adversary dynamic.** Mystique has, across decades, kidnapped her, manipulated her into operations against the X-Men, impersonated her allies to extract information, faked her death twice, and once attempted to broker her as an asset to an external party. Subject has, in turn, hit her hard enough to put her down for issues at a time, refused to mourn her apparent deaths, and publicly disowned her on more than one occasion.

**Why she is the most dangerous person alive to subject.** Because no one else can produce the regression — the moment where subject's adult moral framework is overridden by the eleven-year-old who needed her foster mother to be a foster mother. Mystique exploits this knowingly and without compunction.

**Leverage.** Mystique knows where the body is buried because she helped bury it. She knows the Cody chronology, the Danvers planning, every operational detail of subject's pre-X-Men life. An adversary who acquired Mystique — or her files, or Destiny's diaries — would acquire subject in effect.

---

### Sinister (Nathaniel Essex) — The Genome Threat

**History.** Background presence across the Gambit-history arc; concrete antagonist throughout the Krakoan/*Sins of Sinister* era. Sinister covets her absorption mutation as a genetic asset.

**Dynamics.** Cold, predatory, scientific. He is the adversary who would not bother to manipulate her — he would take a tissue sample. Subject reads him as the inversion of every authority figure she has ever attached to: charisma replaced by appetite, container replaced by consumer.

**Trust / safety.** Zero. She has been visibly hostile to him in Council sessions in a way she modulates with no one else.

**Failure mode.** He is the rare adversary for whom her standard defenses (charm, flirtation, hard physical hit) are useless. He does not respond to the surface; he does not flinch at the hit; he simply has more time than she does.

**Leverage.** He has, at minimum, tissue. He may have her in clone-stock somewhere. The possibility that there is *another her* — uncontaminated by Danvers, uncontaminated by trauma — destabilizes her self-concept in a way she has not metabolized.

---

### The Shadow King (Amahl Farouk) — The Possessor Archetype

**History.** Muir Island Saga (*Uncanny X-Men* #278–280, 1991) — the Shadow King colonized half the team; subject was among the affected.

**Dynamics.** He is the externalization of her worst internal experience: a foreign mind that takes the wheel. Their relationship is purely adversarial, but it is *structured* adversarial — she has a specific protocol for him (engage from distance, do not let him into the mind, lethal-force authorization).

**Failure mode / leverage.** Any telepathic adversary capable of impersonating internal voices can briefly convince her she is experiencing an absorbed-psyche intrusion rather than an attack. The first thirty seconds of a Shadow King-style assault are her most vulnerable interval; she does not know whether to fight or to internally negotiate.

---

### Vargas — The Physical Equal Who Killed Friends

**History.** *X-Treme X-Men* (Claremont, early 2000s). Anti-mutant operative with no powers and physical capability sufficient to match top-tier X-Men. Killed Psylocke; nearly killed subject.

**Dynamics.** Pure operational rival. No psychic component, no relational baggage. He is significant in her file because he is the adversary who taught her she is not invulnerable even with Danvers's gifts — and the encounter sits in her threat library as the prototype for *normal humans who can kill her.*

---

### Sentinels and the institutional-anti-mutant apparatus

Listed as a class. Subject's response to Sentinels and to Sentinel-program-adjacent figures (Bastion, Trask lineage, Orchis in the modern era) is one of the few areas where her affect runs *cold* rather than hot. She fights them with a precision and absence of banter that is characterologically unusual. Diagnostic: this is the one threat class against which she has no ambivalence and therefore no charm.

---

### Selene, Apocalypse, Onslaught, the cosmic tier

Encountered, fought, survived. None occupies a personal slot in her file; she relates to them as institutional problems rather than as people. Apocalypse in the Krakoan era has produced more interpersonal weather than the others because of his Council presence, but even there she registers him as a *fact of the environment* rather than as an adversary with a face.

---

## III. ENEMIES OF THE PAST WHO BECAME SOMETHING ELSE

### The Brotherhood — Pyro, Avalanche, Blob, Destiny

Her *first team.* She fought alongside them under Mystique against the Avengers, against the X-Men, against the United States government. Every one of them has subsequently been a colleague (Pyro on Cable's team; Avalanche/Blob in various roster shuffles; Destiny is her foster mother and a posthumous presence on Krakoa). Subject's pattern: she does not stay enemies with people she has worked with. The category is unstable for her by temperament.

### Wolverine — The Threatened Murder That Became Brotherhood

He drew claws on her in *Uncanny X-Men* #171 and made the kill-on-sight position explicit. She accepted it as fair. Two decades later he is among the small handful of people whose judgment she takes as final. The arc is exemplary: she walks toward the people with most reason to hate her, and the durable ones come around. Wolverine is the proof of the method.

---

## IV. CROSS-CUTTING OBSERVATIONS

**The intimacy/enmity gradient is shallow for her.** People migrate across it. Magneto goes from enemy to lover-adjacent to colleague; Mystique goes from mother to enemy to mother to enemy on a cycle measured in months; Wolverine goes from would-be executioner to brother. The shallowness is itself diagnostic — her attachment system does not maintain hard category walls because her formative environment did not maintain them (Mystique was the woman who loved her *and* the terrorist who deployed her; the foster home was warm *and* moral inversion).

**The unrepairable category is small and specific.** Cody (dead). Danvers (the act cannot be undone). Sinister (no relational substrate to repair). These three are the file's hard ceilings.

**The leverage matrix.** A hostile party seeking maximum behavioral control over subject would: (a) acquire or impersonate Mystique; (b) threaten Gambit; (c) raise the Danvers question publicly; (d) introduce a credible touch-restoration offer with hidden cost. In descending order of operational reliability and ascending order of subtlety. The fourth is the one she has the least defense against because it is indistinguishable, at first contact, from her deepest legitimate wish.

**The protective matrix.** Her core defenders, in the order they would actually mobilize: Gambit, Storm, Wolverine (legacy and current incarnations), Kitty Pryde, Nightcrawler, Magneto (in the operational sense), and — *do not under-weight* — herself. She is, by the current era, her own most reliable defender, which is not a sentence the file could have written in 1985.


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## 0. Frame

Subject presents two distinct power-strata stacked on a deep skills layer: (a) the **native mutation** — involuntary bioelectric absorption via dermal contact — and (b) a **derivative permanent loadout** acquired through the Carol Danvers absorption (Avengers Annual #10, 1981) and held for roughly the next two decades of publication time. Beneath both sits a third layer the file must not underweight: a **trained operator skillset** that long predates either power's stabilization and is what actually keeps her alive on most missions. Each layer must be read both functionally (what it does) and symptomatically (what its shape says about the person). The central thesis of this section: subject's powers are not separable from her injury. They *are* the injury, expressed as physics.

---

## 1. The Native Mutation — Absorption

### 1.1 Mechanism

On skin-to-skin contact, an involuntary transfer initiates from donor → subject. The transferred matter is, in observed order of onset:

1. **Kinetic life-force / vitality** — donor weakens, subject is energized; first to register, within ~1 second of contact.
2. **Memory** — episodic and procedural; arrives in flood form, not query form, and is not initially sortable. Subject reports it as "noise" before it resolves into discrete recollections (Claremont, recurring).
3. **Psychic template** — affective signature, characteristic verbal register, mannerisms, values. This is the dangerous layer: it can colonize her ego if input volume or duration is sufficient.
4. **Powers** — if donor is super-powered, the relevant ability transfers with the template. Mutants transfer the mutation; non-mutant empowered individuals transfer the relevant capacity (Thor's strength and worthiness, Ms. Marvel's flight and durability, Sunfire's plasma, etc.).

The transfer is **bidirectional in effect, unidirectional in flow** — the donor *loses* what subject *gains*, for the duration. Donor recovery time scales nonlinearly with contact duration: a graze costs the donor seconds of orientation; a held contact costs minutes-to-hours of consciousness; a sustained contact (Cody Robbins, ~unknown but extended; Ms. Marvel, ~minute-class) produces coma or permanent dispossession. There is no documented case of subject *returning* what she has taken by reverse contact; this asymmetry matters psychologically (see §5).

### 1.2 Onset and the volitional gate
