At manifestation (Cody Robbins event, age ~thirteen) and for the entire Claremont era, the power has **no volitional gate at baseline.** Contact = transfer. This is the canonical fact and the engine of the character's tragedy: there is no "off."

Across decades, several partial controls have appeared and lapsed:
- **Brief power-loss windows** following high-load events or external resets (post-*X-Men* #171 Carey arc; post-*M-Day* dynamics in some continuities).
- **Mike Carey's *X-Men: Legacy* arc (≈2008–2010):** sustained volitional gating achieved through what is effectively guided ego-integration — she learns to "shelve" the absorbed psyches and, by extension, throttle the input channel. This is the first time control is presented as **psychological work**, not external device.
- **Mr. and Mrs. X (2018) onward:** stable enough control to consent to physical intimacy; the gate is real but not absolute and remains effort-loaded under stress.
- **Krakoan era:** control is operational, with documented slips under extreme exertion or emotional load — a clinically realistic profile (a regulated chronic deficit is not a cured one).

### 1.3 Range, vector, latency

- **Range:** contact only. No field effect. Clothing fully blocks the transfer; thickness is irrelevant — the variable is dermal coverage, not insulation. This is why her uniform is **categorical** (full-coverage) rather than **graded** (heavy).
- **Vector:** any uncovered skin surface on either party; lips and hands are the highest-traffic vectors in the record because they are the highest-traffic vectors in human intimacy generally, which is the cruelty of the case.
- **Latency:** sub-second for vitality; 1–3 seconds for memory onset; psychic template lags, often minutes, sometimes hours; powers register concurrent with vitality.
- **Decay:** acquired powers and personae decay over hours to weeks for incidental absorptions; permanent for sustained ones (Danvers). Memories decay slowly and incompletely.

### 1.4 Ceiling and overload

The absorption has demonstrated near-omega ceiling under specific conditions: in *Uncanny X-Men* #185 and again in event-scale arcs, mass-absorption events have driven her power readout into class-Omega-adjacent territory. The constraint is **stability,** not magnitude. She can hold more than she can metabolize. Overload presentations:

- **Psychotic-spectrum episode** after Magneto absorption (*X-Men* #25, 1993): she displays his pathologies, not just his powers.
- **Dissociative displacement** after Danvers absorption (*Uncanny X-Men* #150–158, peaking #269): donor identity intermittently runs the body.
- **Sensory and affective flooding** after any large-template absorption: she reports the donor's grief, fear, or rage as her own and cannot sort it in real time.

The functional ceiling, therefore, is *containment capacity,* and containment capacity is a function of her ego strength, which is a function of how integrated she is at the moment of contact. **Her power scales with her psychological wellness.** This is the unusual and clinically resonant fact of her mutation.

---

## 2. The Danvers Loadout (acquired, long-tenured)

For roughly two decades of publication time, subject carried a permanent Kree-hybrid physiology grafted onto her own:

- **Superhuman strength** (lifting strength in the class-50-to-class-75-ton range at peak, scaling with continuity).
- **Flight** (atmospheric, high subsonic; substack hypersonic at exertion).
- **Durability / near-invulnerability** — small-arms fire trivial, missile-tier impact survivable.
- **Enhanced senses and reflexes** at Kree-hybrid baseline.
- **The seventh sense** (Danvers's precognitive intuition, attenuated in subject).

**Granular use-pattern.** She used the loadout *instrumentally*, not expressively. She did not stunt-fly. She did not display strength gratuitously. She used flight for ingress/egress and to extract teammates, used strength to hit hard once rather than spar, used durability to *interpose* — flying into the path of attacks aimed at others. The pattern is consistent across hundreds of issues: **the Danvers powers are deployed as a shield, almost never as a sword.** This is a guilt-loadout. She uses the stolen ability to protect the people whose protection she has not earned. Reparation expressed as combat doctrine.

**Loss.** The loadout was eventually shed (Carey-era resets and reboots variously dispose of it). Subject did not mourn its loss in the record; she mourned *Cody* and she mourned *Carol*, but she did not mourn flight. Diagnostic: the powers were never hers in any felt sense.

---

## 3. Borrowed Suites — Catalogue and Pattern

A non-exhaustive list of confirmed significant absorptions, by function:

- **Wolverine** (multiple occasions): healing factor, sensorium, claws-as-bone-projection in some depictions. She has used his healing factor to survive otherwise lethal injuries; she has used his sensorium for tracking.
- **Magneto** (*X-Men* #25, 1993): magnetokinesis at near-master tier, plus his pathologies. She is at her most dangerous and least herself in this state.
- **Gambit** (*X-Men* #41): kinetic charging of objects; she also absorbed his hidden past, which is the rupture of the courtship's first phase.
- **Sunfire, Cannonball, Iceman, Colossus, Nightcrawler, Storm, Cyclops, Polaris, et al.** — virtually every long-tenured teammate at one point or another, usually in combat triage.
- **Sentry-tier or cosmic-scale figures** in event arcs — handled briefly, never stably.
- **Non-mutant humans** in incidental contact: memory floods, vitality drains; no power gain.

The **pattern of choice** is the diagnostic part. When she absorbs *voluntarily* (Carey era forward), she selects teammates whose powers are protective or extricatory — healing factors, teleportation, force fields, telepathic shielding. She does not select for offense unless the tactical situation makes offense the only path to extraction. **She absorbs to save, not to kill.** The Carol Danvers incident remains the categorical exception, and it remains the wound.

---

## 4. The Operator Skillset (the layer that actually keeps her alive)

Stripped of every power, subject is still a high-tier field operator. The skillset is composite — Mystique-and-Destiny tradecraft, Brotherhood combatives, Xavier-school formal training, and four decades of mission-volume reps.

- **Hand-to-hand:** Brotherhood-era street brawler upgraded through Xavier-school structured combat; later, after Danvers's Kree training imprinted procedurally, a trained military fighter with leverage-and-targeting discipline. Retained as muscle memory even after power-shift events.
- **Tradecraft:** infiltration, surveillance evasion, false-identity maintenance — Mystique's pedagogy. She is good at not being seen when she chooses, and she chooses often.
- **Tactical reading:** rapid threat-assessment, terrain exploitation, exfil-planning bias. She thinks about exits before entries, which is both training and characterology.
- **Aerial combat doctrine** (Danvers era): three-dimensional maneuvering, ramming-as-attack, payload-class interposition.
- **Field leadership:** emerges late (post-Carey), consolidates in the Krakoan era. Lateral, terse, decision-fast; she does not deliberate publicly, she calls the play and moves.
- **Interpersonal read** — the under-appreciated skill. Partly Mystique training, partly the simple cumulative effect of having been inside dozens of other people's heads. She reads micro-expression, tone, posture, and tell at a rate consistent with someone who has had the inside view of how those signals are generated. This is her edge on the Quiet Council.

The skillset is **the only layer of her capability that is fully and uncontestedly hers.** Note the psychological weight of that fact.

---

## 5. Limits — the categorical and the contingent

**Categorical limits** (do not bend, in the canonical record):

- Power requires dermal contact. No field, no projection, no remote action.
- Transfer is uncontrolled at baseline; control is recent, effortful, and unreliable under load.
- Acquired powers fade for incidental absorptions; only sustained absorption produces permanent acquisition, and sustained absorption catastrophically harms the donor.
- She cannot return what she has taken by reverse contact. The transfer is one-way.
- She cannot selectively absorb — power without memory, memory without affect. It comes as a bundle.

**Contingent limits** (situational, exploitable):

- Coverage failure: any garment breach is a vulnerability vector. She compensates with redundancy (long gloves under sleeves, high collars, full-length costumes) — a costuming discipline that reads, to the trained observer, as obsessive.
- Forced contact attacks: opponents who know her can attempt to *make her absorb them* as an offensive vector (overloading her with hostile psyche). Documented multiple times. She has learned to refuse contact even when contact would win the fight.
- Telepathic vulnerability: a head full of other people's templates is a head full of attack surface. Telepaths can use absorbed personae against her.
- Emotional load reduces volitional gating. Stress reopens the channel.

---

## 6. Growth Curve

- **Phase I (manifestation through Brotherhood, ~age 13–17):** no control, no integration; power used as weapon under Mystique's direction.
- **Phase II (X-Men entry through Australia/Genosha, mid-80s through early 90s):** no control, defensive use only; Danvers loadout carries most of her combat function; absorbed-psyche containment is the dominant intrapsychic task.
- **Phase III (Lobdell/Nicieza, mid-late 90s):** stabilization of identity around the X-Men; powers unchanged in mechanism; Gambit-courtship years define the *near-touch* ritual repertoire.
- **Phase IV (Carey era, mid-2000s through 2010):** the first real volitional integration; control is achieved as a *byproduct of ego work*, not as a discrete acquisition. This is the most important growth event in her history.
- **Phase V (Krakoan/modern):** consented intimacy stable; field control reliable; field leadership consolidated; slips under extreme load remain.

The arc is real and unusually well-drawn for a long-running serial character: the power has been *therapy-shaped*, and her clinical trajectory and her power-control trajectory are the same curve.

---

## 7. Signature Applications

- **The pull-the-glove-off neutralization.** Late-fight, against an opponent she cannot defeat by force, she removes a glove and ends it. The gesture has acquired iconographic weight in the record because everyone — opponent, teammate, reader — recognizes what it costs her. She uses it sparingly; she uses it deliberately; she has used it on figures up to and including world-tier threats. It is her **nuclear option** and she treats it as one.
- **Triage absorption.** Quick contact with a downed teammate to *take* the wound (via healing factor borrow) or *take* the load (to remove a possessed teammate from play). She has done this dozens of times across the record. It hurts her every time; she does it anyway.
- **Interposition flight (Danvers era).** Bodying the incoming hit aimed at a teammate. Frequent. Diagnostic.
- **The combat-grade flirt.** Verbal warmth as battlefield tool — disarming opponents who cannot square the Southern-belle register with the woman who can drop them. Pure psyops, weaponized character.
- **Council-room read.** Modern era: she sits silent and watches; when she speaks, she speaks short and decisive. The interpersonal-read skill turned political.

---

## 8. Symptom-as-Signature

Read the power against the person and the convergence is total.

- **The mutation enforces the wound.** Her central injury — categorical denial of affective touch (Sailer et al., 2016, on the orbitofrontal/putamen reward substrate of pleasant touch and its role in social bond maintenance) — is not a side effect of the power. It *is* the power. Most mutants have a mutation and a life; her mutation *is* the life-shape. The clinical fact (chronic deprivation of a reward-circuit-recruiting biological need) and the narrative fact (cannot touch) are the same fact.
- **The uniform is the prosthesis.** Full-coverage clothing is medical countermeasure (a substitute for the missing inhibitory pathway) and characterological armor (isolation of affect, externalized). The defense and the necessity are the same garment.
- **Acquired powers as somatic guilt.** The Danvers loadout was used as a shield for two decades, never as a trophy. The body she had was contraband, and she spent the contraband paying restitution.
- **Control as integration.** That volitional gating arrived through ego-work and not through device or genetic patch is the cleanest possible statement of the case: **her power is governed by her selfhood.** When she is whole, the channel closes. When she fragments, it opens. The mutation does not metaphorize the psychology; it *is* the psychology made physical.
- **The pull-the-glove gesture as the whole character in one motion.** She removes the prosthesis; she absorbs the harm; she carries the donor inside her afterward; she goes home alone. Every component of the file is in that gesture.
- **The skillset as the only unstolen self.** The combat training, the tradecraft, the read — these are the only capabilities she has not taken from someone else. It is not an accident that the modern, integrated Rogue leads from this layer.

The file's working summary: **her abilities are an exact diagram of her injury, and the long arc of her control over them is an exact diagram of her healing.** Treat the powers section and the psychology section as two readings of one document.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT — SUBJECT: ROGUE

*Cross-reference: §1 History; §3 Psychological; §5 Personality. This section maps the* how *— mechanics of decision, motion, money, gear, and the small repeatable signatures that identify the subject in the field even when she is not in costume.*

---

## 1. DECISION ARCHITECTURE

**Latency profile.** Subject is a fast operator on tactical decisions (<2 seconds to engage in combat, often <1 in defense of a teammate) and a slow operator on relational ones (months to years on intimacy thresholds; the Gambit courtship ran a decade before consummation). The asymmetry is diagnostic: tactical decisions activate trained pathways laid down by Mystique-era field instruction and twenty-plus years of X-Men operations; relational decisions activate the wounded substrate, and she stalls. Files analyzing her response times to mixed stimuli will see this bifurcation cleanly.

**Decision sequence under threat.** Observed pattern across the published record: (a) *triangulate the civilians* — her head turns first to non-combatants in the area, not to the threat; (b) *locate the teammate most exposed* — eyes go to the one without invulnerability before her own engagement begins; (c) *select absorption target* — if there is a power-class opponent, she designates them for skin-contact takedown; (d) *commit.* Steps (a) and (b) happen pre-engagement and are visible as a characteristic two-beat head-scan even out of costume.

**Decision sequence under social/political pressure.** Slower, three-pass: she will (a) state a strong position publicly, usually loyalty-framed; (b) privately revise toward pragmatism after consultation with one trusted peer (historically Storm; latterly Gambit); (c) act on the revised position while letting the original public statement stand as cover. This is *Mystique-trained tradecraft repurposed for legitimate institutions* — she learned compartmentation from a terrorist mother and now uses it to govern.

**Risk tolerance.** Asymmetric. Extremely high tolerance for *physical* risk to her own body — she will run into ordnance, take a hit meant for a teammate, hold contact with a hostile telepath knowing she will absorb a fragment of their psyche. Extremely *low* tolerance for *relational* risk — she will not initiate an intimate gesture without redundant guarantees of safety. The somatic guilt (§2 of the workup) inverts the normal risk hierarchy: her body is *expendable to her in a way the relationship is not.*

**Heuristics observable in repeated decisions.**
- *Run toward the wronged party.* (Defection to X-Men; later attempts to make peace with the Avengers regarding Danvers.) She trusts injured parties more than uninjured ones — the injured have a comprehensible motive structure.
- *Take command when no one else will.* She does not seek authority; she occupies vacated authority and is reluctant to relinquish it once occupied. The Quiet Council seat fits this pattern, as does her field leadership across multiple team configurations.
- *Distrust the offered gift.* Anything given without demand is treated as a probable hook. Mystique taught this directly.
- *Touch is the last option, never the first.* In combat she uses absorption as the closer, not the opener. This is both tactically sound (telegraphs her intent only at the end) and characterologically inevitable.

---

## 2. COMBAT TRADECRAFT

**Standing power-set assumptions for operational planning.** The file must distinguish *eras.* Pre-Danvers: absorption only, no enhanced physicals. Danvers-derivative era (~1981 through mid-2000s): Class-100 strength, flight, near-invulnerability, ambient durability sufficient to take starship-grade ordnance. Post-Danvers-reset eras: variable, dependent on most recent absorption; baseline reverts toward unenhanced. Krakoan-era: trained volitional control, broad retained skill library, on-demand strength/flight via deliberate residual access. The *operating doctrine* shifted across eras but the *signature* did not.

**Engagement doctrine — Danvers-powered period.** Functioned as a flying brick with a finishing move. Standard engagement: close at flight speed, deliver a single decisive blow, follow up if needed. She did *not* enjoy the brick role and it shows in the choreography — minimal flourish, no acrobatic grandstanding, no taunting (unlike, e.g., Wolverine's combat persona). She gets it over with.

**Engagement doctrine — absorption-primary period.** Skin contact as terminal sanction. Approach pattern: verbal engagement (the flirtatious register weaponized as distraction — see §4); glove removal as a visible *threat-display* rather than a concealed move; brief contact for incapacitation; longer only under extremity. She has demonstrated calibrated dose-control across decades — capable of seconds-long contact that yields knockout without permanent damage, sustained contact only against existential threats (Magneto in *X-Men* #25 being the canonical extremity).

**Glove-removal as ritual.** The act of pulling a glove off with her teeth — repeated across artists and decades — is functionally identical to a soldier chambering a round in plain view. It is *deliberately observable.* She wants the opponent to know what is coming. This serves three purposes: (i) it offers them a chance to surrender or flee, satisfying her guilt structure; (ii) it provokes panic responses that degrade their combat performance; (iii) it allows her to defer the act she does not want to commit. The ritual is slow on purpose.

**Use of teammates as absorption sources (consensual buffing).** Carey-era and later: she will request brief contact with a teammate to acquire their power-set for a defined operation. Observed protocol: explicit verbal consent, brief planned contact, defined duration of borrowed power, debriefing if any psychic residue surfaces. She is unusually formal about this — the legacy of having taken without asking once.

**Aerial behavior.** When flight-capable, she patrols low and slow (treetop-to-rooftop band), not high-altitude. Two reasons: better situational awareness of civilians, and — inferred — a residual ground-orientation from a swamp-country childhood; she does not love altitude the way Carol Danvers did. Files comparing flight telemetry between the two would show this clearly.

**Defensive tells.** When struck unexpectedly, she rotates her body to receive impact on her left side. Inferred from repeated combat panels: a long-standing protective bias toward the right hand (her glove-removal hand and primary contact instrument). Damage to the right glove is treated as a higher-priority loss than damage elsewhere on the suit; she will disengage to re-cover it.

---

## 3. WARDROBE, GEAR, AND THE PROSTHETIC PERIMETER

**The bodysuit is medical equipment.** Treat as PPE, not costume. Standing requirements: full coverage from jaw to fingertip to toe; high collar; gloves that close past the wrist; no exposed midriff in operational rigs (the various midriff-baring variants in the published art are off-duty or stylized; her operational suits cover). Material requirements derived from observed performance: tear-resistant, abrasion-resistant, retains integrity after impact, dries quickly (she has fought in marine and jungle environments without compromise). Likely composition in-universe: unstable molecules / Krakoan biofiber / equivalent. Real-world analog for surveillance purposes: think high-coverage athletic compression layer plus tactical outer.

**Redundancy.** She does not operate without backup gloves. Multiple pairs on her person at all times — established repeatedly in quiet panels where she changes them after a contact event. Treat *glove inventory* as the single most reliable forensic indicator that a location is hers: spare pairs in vehicles, in lockers, in the kitchen drawer, on the nightstand.

**Hair management.** The white forelock is uncovered and uncovered-on-purpose: it is the most reliable visual identifier of the subject and she has never sought to disguise it for long. When she has gone undercover, the forelock has been dyed or covered — and the act of covering it visibly distresses her on-panel. Inference: the streak is identity-marker, not vanity. It appeared at mutation onset (or, per some accounts, after the Cody event) and functions as her external monument to what happened.

**Off-duty wardrobe.** Long sleeves year-round, regardless of climate. Gloves in any room with people; bare hands only in solitude or in confirmed-safe company (Gambit, post-control; medical personnel under protocol). Sleeve hems are pulled toward the knuckle as a self-soothing motion — a tic visible in countless panels.

**Weapons.** Minimal personal armament historically; the body is the weapon. In post-power-reset periods she has carried small-caliber sidearms and edged weapons competently, reflecting Mystique-era training. She is not a marksman of note and does not pretend to be. She *does* train with knives — Brotherhood legacy — and the file should note that an unarmed Rogue is not an unarmed combatant.

**Communications.** Standard X-comm hardware in each era; nothing idiosyncratic. Notable absence: she does not run private back-channels (compare Mystique, who runs many; compare Gambit, who has Guild channels). Her communications discipline is institutional, not personal — another marker of her conscious refusal of the Brotherhood operational mode.

---

## 4. SOCIAL TRADECRAFT — THE FLIRTATIOUS REGISTER AS METHOD

**The accent and the sugar.** The Mississippi cadence is real (residual from childhood) but *amplified* in operational contexts. Volume of "sugah," "darlin'," and the soft-vowel register correlates positively with threat assessment: the warmer she sounds, the more dangerous the situation. Surveillance baseline should index drawl-thickness against environmental stressors; deviations from the curve are tells.

**Functions of the register.**
- *Disarmament.* Opponents — especially male opponents — consistently misread the Southern-belle presentation as performative softness and underestimate engagement timing. She knows this and uses it.
- *Distance-management.* The flirtatious surface holds people at a precisely calibrated middle distance — close enough to read, far enough to not require contact. It is a *spacing tool.*
- *Reaction-formation surface.* (Per §3 of the workup.) The performed warmth manages an inability to deliver actual warmth.
- *Consent-signalling channel.* With trusted intimates, modulation of the register (dropping the performance, going quiet, dropping the accent toward neutral) signals real, unmediated address. The people who know her track the *absence* of the drawl as the signal.

**Negotiation style.** Direct under the surface charm. She does not bluff well on substance — she will commit early to a position and defend it — but she bluffs *posture* expertly. Opposing negotiators frequently report believing she had leverage she did not have. Quiet Council voting record (where observable) is consistent: she takes early positions and holds them, with one or two visible revisions across the entire run.

**Mentorship as deployment.** She *uses* mentorship of younger X-Men operationally as well as therapeutically. Reads the new mutant; identifies a competency to develop; runs them through low-stakes operations as graduated exposure. The mentees become loyal lieutenants she can call on years later. This is institution-building via the back door — the legitimate analog of Mystique's recruitment patterns, with the predation excised.

---

## 5. INTELLIGENCE TRADECRAFT — THE PSYCHIC RESIDUE

**Absorption as collection.** Every prolonged contact has yielded the donor's full skillset and memory set. Over four decades this has accreted into an extraordinary unindexed intelligence library: Magneto's strategic thinking, Gambit's Guild knowledge, multiple telepaths' fragments, Danvers's military and intelligence training, fragments of every X-Man she has ever touched in extremity. She does not have full volitional access to this library but it surfaces under matched-stimulus conditions.

**Operational consequence.** She is an unreliable but very deep HUMINT asset *on herself.* A skilled interrogator on her side can prompt-retrieve fragments she does not consciously know she holds; a hostile interrogator who knew the architecture could in principle do the same. She compartments this risk by avoiding telepathic contact with parties she does not trust — a discipline established after the early Danvers-personality crises.

**Tradecraft she carries from absorbed sources.** Lock-picking and cardistry (Gambit). Strategic-operational planning at theater scale (Magneto, Danvers). Counter-surveillance and pattern-of-life evasion (Mystique by direct training, reinforced by absorbed fragments). Field medicine, basic (multiple sources). Languages: subject demonstrably comprehends fragments of languages she never studied — almost certainly residue from absorbed donors; her active production is far weaker than her comprehension, consistent with stored rather than learned acquisition.

**Counter-intelligence posture.** High. She does not discuss operations in unsecured spaces; she does not write personal logs of substance (no diary discipline established in the record, which is itself a discipline); she does not retain souvenirs of operations beyond a small number of sentimental items associated with Gambit. The *absence of personal records* across forty years of in-universe activity is itself a tradecraft signature.

---

## 6. FINANCES AND RESOURCING

**Personal finances.** Modest and opaque. No documented wealth accumulation independent of institutional support. Pre-X-Men: Brotherhood-supplied, essentially stipendiary. X-Men era: Xavier Institute housing, board, equipment, transport. Krakoan era: post-economic by design of the polity. Across all eras she has been *resourced by institutions* and has not built a personal financial base.

**This is diagnostic.** Compare Gambit (Guild wealth, multiple caches, false identities with bank access). Compare Storm (royal stipend periods, occasional treasure-based assets). Subject has consistently declined the opportunity to accumulate. Inference: independence from institutional housing would require her to *touch* a landlord, a banker, a clerk; institutional life provides social infrastructure that pre-clears those contacts. The dependence is structural, not characterological — but it has shaped her relationship to authority (she has remained reliant on the institutions she serves, which has made her loyal and made her vulnerable to institutional capture).

**Material baseline.** Minimal. Operates light. Possessions across known residences are catalogable on one page: clothing inventory heavy on coverage garments; a small jewelry set (much of it Gambit-gifted in later years, kept rather than worn); a small library skewed toward Southern literature and practical manuals; no art collection; no electronics beyond utility. She does not nest. Spaces she lives in feel transient even when she has occupied them for years. Trace evidence: glove pairs in drawers; sleeve-fiber on furniture corners; *no fingerprints on surfaces in living areas she frequents alone* — she habitually wipes contact surfaces, a tic that began as decontamination and persists as ritual.

**Resource access via network.** What she lacks in personal finance she has in calls-she-can-make. Through forty years of pro-social labor she has built a deep relational ledger: she can request a safe house from any of several X-Men diaspora figures; medical care from multiple sources; transport from Guild contacts via Gambit; sanctuary in Wakanda via Storm-era ties. The network is the wealth.

---

## 7. INFRASTRUCTURE AND PATTERN OF LIFE

**Residences across eras.** Caldecott County household (fled). Mystique/Destiny safe houses (multiple, transient, deliberately untraceable by Brotherhood doctrine). Xavier's mansion (her longest stable residence; multiple rooms across reconstructions; consistently chosen low-floor and near-exit). Australian outback base (Reavers-era, group housing). Muir Island. Various team facilities. Krakoan housing. The Mr. and Mrs. X domestic interval — significant because it is the first residence she has chosen for herself rather than been assigned.

**Consistent residential preferences.** Ground floor or near-exit. Window access. Near a body of water when possible (swamp-country residue). Minimal shared bathroom contact surfaces. *Door always closed but unlocked* — she wants the option of egress, not the imposition of barrier. A bedside light kept on at low setting through sleep periods (inferred from repeated panel evidence).

**Sleep architecture.** Disturbed. Documented nightmares across multiple decades and writers — content typically Danvers-themed, Cody-themed, or Mystique-themed. Wakes early. Will tolerate co-sleeping only with confirmed-safe partners under heavy fabric barrier; even then, position preference is back-to-back, not face-to-face, and not skin-contact-adjacent.

**Daily rhythm in stable periods.** Early riser. Coffee strong and black (no shared-cup risk). Physical training in the morning — flight patterns when capable, strength work otherwise, sustained because the body is the instrument. Mid-day: institutional duties, teaching, command meetings. Evening: small social engagement with a defined inner circle, terminating early. Night: long solitude. The rhythm is monastic dressed as Southern.

**Movement and transport.** Prefers self-powered transport when flight-capable — does not like being a passenger. When grounded, prefers driving herself (motorcycles documented across eras; she likes the helmet-and-leathers configuration because it is *coverage that reads as style*). Avoids public transit. Avoids crowded elevators. Will take stairs by preference.

**Public spaces.** Walks the perimeter of rooms; does not cut through crowds. Orders food at counters by gesturing where possible. Pays in cash where institutional credit is not available. Holds doors with her foot, not her hand. Reads the contact-surfaces of every room she enters within the first ten seconds and unconsciously positions to minimize incidental brushes — a learned spatial competence that observers consistently misread as "graceful."

---

## 8. SIGNATURE OPERATIONAL TELLS

A surveillance file's value is in the *small repeatable signatures* by which the subject can be identified even when disguised, displaced, or impersonated. The following are the high-confidence Rogue markers:

1. **The two-beat civilian-then-teammate head scan** before engagement.
2. **Glove removal with teeth, right hand**, slow, with eye contact.
3. **Drawl-thickness inversely tracking comfort** — warmer she sounds, more dangerous the moment.
4. **Sleeve-hem pulled toward knuckle** as a self-soothing tic, both hands, alternating.
5. **Forelock left visible** even when full disguise would be operationally preferable; covering it visibly distresses her.
6. **Spare gloves cached in every personal space.**
7. **Surfaces wiped of fingerprints** in personal residences — a decontamination ritual that outlived its original purpose.
8. **Door unlocked, closed; bedside light at low** through sleep.
9. **Back-to-back co-sleeping** with intimates; never face-to-face skin-adjacent.
10. **Coffee black, no shared cups, no shared utensils** — across all eras, all settings.
11. **Drops the drawl toward neutral** as a real-address signal with trusted intimates; the *absence* of performance is the affection.
12. **Left-side rotation to receive impact**, protecting the right (contact) hand.
13. **Refuses passenger seat when self-transport is available.**
14. **Will not initiate handshake or hug**, ever; will accept fabric-mediated contact from trusted parties only.
15. **Mentions Mystique only in third-person past tense** in formal settings, even when Mystique is a current operational concern — a verbal compartmentation tic.
16. **Will run toward the party she has most recently wronged** rather than away. If a file shows Rogue moving *toward* a known antagonist with no tactical reason, the operational read is reparation, not aggression.
17. **No personal written records.** Forty years of operations, essentially no paper trail outside institutional logs.
18. **Reads the room's contact-surfaces within ten seconds of entry**; observable as a brief eye-sweep at doorways.

---

## 9. OPERATIONAL VULNERABILITIES (DEFENSIVE NOTES)

For the file's protective use, not its predatory one:

- **Mystique-mediated approaches** bypass her standing skepticism more reliably than any other vector. Any operation in which Mystique appears as intermediary, source, or apparent victim should be treated as compromised at the planning stage.
- **Threats to Gambit** will collapse her decision latency from slow-relational to fast-tactical and degrade her strategic judgment. She becomes a precision instrument with a damaged guidance system.
- **Sustained absorption events** under combat conditions can trigger dissociative episodes lasting hours to days. Operations requiring her absorption capability should be planned with explicit post-event recovery windows and a designated psychic-stabilization contact.
- **Touch-themed taunts from telepathic opponents** are her single most effective psychological weapon-vector. Standing counsel: she should not engage Class-Omega telepaths solo.
- **Institutional dependence** is her financial and logistical exposure. A coordinated effort to delegitimize or dissolve her current institutional home (as has happened repeatedly across X-Men history) leaves her unusually under-resourced relative to peers, and she will accept aid from suboptimal sources to remain operational.

---

*End section. Cross-reference forward to behavioral baselines (somatic micro-patterns) and relational mapping (the Gambit dyad, the Mystique transference, the Storm anchor) in subsequent sections.*


## Worldview & Operational Code

# Worldview & Operational Code — SUBJECT: ROGUE

*A reconstruction of the belief system as it operates, not as the subject would articulate it. Where the subject's stated creed and her revealed creed diverge, both are recorded.*

---

## 1. First Principles — The Substrate Beliefs

The subject's worldview rests on four axioms, all empirically derived from her own body and history rather than from any text or teacher. They precede and constrain every higher-order belief she holds.

**Axiom I: Contact is consequential.** Most people hold "actions have consequences" as a moral abstraction; subject holds it as a sensory law. Every skin-to-skin event in her life has produced measurable, often catastrophic, downstream effect — a comatose boy, a stolen woman, a maddened magnetar, a Cajun's confession. She does not believe in casual interaction the way ordinary people do, because she has no neurological category for it. This generalizes outward: she expects *every* act to leave an imprint somewhere, and she budgets her behavior accordingly. It is the source of her unusual ethical seriousness and of her near-allergy to flippancy in others when stakes are real.

**Axiom II: The self is permeable.** She knows from direct experience that what she takes to be "her" thoughts can in fact be someone else's, lodged in her cortex without invitation. This produces a worldview in which identity is *defended terrain* rather than given substance. She does not assume coherence in herself or in others; she treats personality as something one has to *hold together* by ongoing effort. The corollary is a peculiar generosity: when she sees someone behaving out of character, her first hypothesis is *intrusion* (mind control, possession, coercion), not malice. She has been there.

**Axiom III: Harm is asymmetric and usually irreversible.** Cody did not wake up because she felt bad. Carol Danvers's life did not return because subject joined the X-Men. The Marauders' victims stayed dead after she learned Gambit's history. Subject does not believe in clean restitution. She believes in *reparation as ongoing labor* — work performed forever on behalf of a debt that cannot be discharged. This makes her a long-game thinker in a way most of her teammates are not.

**Axiom IV: The body is not entirely one's own property.** Hers is partly Carol Danvers's, periodically Magneto's, sometimes a stranger's whose hand she had to grab in a fight. The body is a *site* — leased, contested, occupied. From this comes her distinctive position on bodily autonomy: fierce in defense of *others'* (consent, in any form, is sacred to her in ways that surprise people who only know her flirtatious surface), and oddly fatalistic about her own.

---

## 2. How She Reads the World

**Reading people.** Fast, accurate, somatic. She does not analyze a stranger's face the way an intellectual does; she *gets* them, in the same fractional second a Mississippi cardplayer would have gotten them, augmented by the fact that she has — literally — been inside dozens of minds and so has a calibration set most observers lack. She reads posture before words. She notices what a person does with their hands. She notices what people do with *her* hands — whether they flinch, whether they pretend not to flinch, whether they perform ease. The flinchers she trusts more than the performers; the flinchers are at least honest.

She is unusually unfooled by charm because she runs a charm operation herself and knows the controls. She is unusually unfooled by stoicism because she runs that operation too. She *is* fooled, repeatedly, by people who appear to offer what she has been denied — the containing parental figure, the lover who claims her presence is enough. Mystique exploits this, and Magneto did, and on bad days Gambit does without meaning to. She knows this about herself but the knowing does not fully inoculate her.

**Reading conflict.** Subject sees fights in three categories. *Necessary fights* (defense of the team, defense of mutantkind, defense of a person she has chosen) she enters without hesitation and prefers to finish decisively. *Optional fights* she avoids when she can; she has no taste for sparring or showboating, and the constant low-grade combat banter that some of her teammates indulge is foreign to her — she does not find violence interesting in itself. *Stupid fights* (ego, territory, pride) she will exit by walking away or by ending them with disproportionate force; she does not negotiate inside them.

In combat she defaults to range and force-application — flight, strength, durability — because the alternative (her primary mutation) is psychologically expensive. Every absorption is a memory she will carry and a personality she will have to evict. She uses touch in combat the way a soldier uses a sidearm: when other options fail, and with awareness that she will be the one cleaning up afterward.

**Reading institutions.** Suspicious of all of them, willing to work inside the ones that pass minimum tests. The X-Men passed (just barely, and over time). The Brotherhood failed in retrospect. Krakoa's Quiet Council she joined not because she believed in its mythology but because *somebody* has to do the hard institutional work and she would rather it be her than someone less scrupulous. This is the mature form of a pattern visible from her first defection: she will lend her body to structures she does not philosophically endorse if the alternative is letting worse people run them.

**Reading the world's posture toward mutants.** Realist, not catastrophist. She has lived through enough Sentinel incidents, Genosha-tier atrocities, and ordinary human bigotries to have no illusions about the baseline hostility of the species toward hers. But she does not — unlike Magneto, whose mind she has briefly held — generalize from atrocity to extermination logic. Her Southern-Protestant substrate retains the conviction that individual humans are individually accountable, redeemable, occasionally good. She votes for vigilance, not war.

---

## 3. Trust — The Architecture

Trust, for subject, is not an emotion; it is a *protocol* with stages.

**Stage zero: Cordiality.** Anyone gets it. The "sugah" and the smile cost her nothing and buy her information. It is the lowest-cost surveillance device a person can run, and she runs it constantly. Do not mistake it for warmth.

**Stage one: Operational trust.** Granted to someone who has performed reliably in a defined task — a teammate who held a line, a contact who delivered. Operational trust does not generalize across domains. She will trust a soldier in a firefight without trusting them with a secret.

**Stage two: Confidential trust.** Granted to someone who has demonstrated discretion across multiple unsupervised opportunities. This tier is small: Storm, eventually Kurt, eventually a few others who passed long observation. Gambit holds it despite multiple violations because she has decided — repeatedly, knowingly — to extend it to him.

**Stage three: Containment trust.** The rarest tier. Granted to someone whose presence she finds *holds her together* under load. Storm has held this. Xavier sometimes. Gambit, in marriage, holds it now. Mystique once held it and the loss has never fully healed; subject still gives Mystique chances she would not give anyone else, because the limbic system does not respect later policy. This is the tier subject most needs and most fears, because anyone in it can do damage no other category of person can.

**Revocation.** She is slow to revoke fully. Betrayals tend to demote rather than excommunicate. The exception is betrayals involving the people she has placed in her containment tier — those produce immediate, permanent functional separation, though the underlying affection persists in a quarantined form (see again: Mystique).

---

## 4. Control — Self, Others, Power

**Self-control as supreme value.** Subject lived most of her life as the case study of what happens when self-control fails: the body acts, the other party is destroyed. She has therefore developed an unusual reverence for self-mastery — her own and others'. People who lose their tempers in stupid ways read to her as *dangerous* in a way that other people do not see. People who maintain composure under genuine duress read to her as *kin.* This is part of why she gravitates toward Storm; it is part of why Wolverine, despite the rocky start, eventually earned her loyalty (the berserker frightened her less than his ability to come back from it).

**Control of others.** She does not want it. The mutation has given her involuntary intimate access to other minds and she has hated every minute of it; the experience has produced an unusually clean stance on coercion. She does not manipulate. She *charms* — and there is a real difference, which is that charm announces itself and manipulation hides. She will use force to stop an enemy and authority to direct a team, but she does not run schemes on the people in her life. The Mystique mode of operation — disguise, deception, long-running con — she rejects categorically, and her rejection is one of the load-bearing achievements of her adult character.

**Control of her own power.** The long arc of her life. She began with none, acquired partial volitional control under Carey's tenure, lost it, regained variants of it through Krakoan-era resurrection mechanics, and currently operates as a high-functioning user who can choose. She does not, however, trust the choice fully — the gloves frequently stay on even when they could come off. The somatic memory of involuntary harm is durable. She would rather be safe than free.

**Authority.** She believes authority is necessary, suspects it is usually misused, and concludes that scrupulous people must therefore accept it when offered. This is why she takes leadership — not from ambition but from a sense that ambition is precisely the wrong qualification for the job. Her model of good authority: minimum theater, maximum responsibility, clear accountability, willingness to take the hit personally. Her model of bad authority: charismatic vision detached from operational consequence (she has, with great love and great difficulty, watched several Xaviers and Magnetos demonstrate this).

---

## 5. Risk — How She Calculates

Subject's risk calculus is *asymmetric and idiosyncratic.* She underweights risk to herself and overweights risk to others, especially others who have been brought into proximity by her choices.

**To her own body:** near-fatalistic. She has been killed and resurrected; she has been beaten near death repeatedly; she has walked through the Siege Perilous as a form of voluntary obliteration. She is not suicidal in the active sense, but her threshold for accepting personal physical risk is set well below most of her peers'. Part of this is courage; part of it is the working belief that the body is partly contraband anyway.

**To her psyche:** here she is more careful, because the lessons are vivid. She will refuse absorptions she could perform if the donor's mind is large or unstable enough to colonize her. The decision to absorb is a *clinical* decision for her, with intake and aftermath, not a tactical reflex.

**To her teammates:** conservative, almost protective to a fault. She will accept risk to herself to lower risk to them, but she will not gamble with their bodies the way some commanders will. This makes her a slower decisionmaker in council settings than the pure utilitarians, and a more trusted one.

**To civilians:** absolute. She is the X-Man least likely to accept civilian casualties as the price of a tactical objective. The Mississippi-Protestant substrate again — innocents do not get spent.

**To Gambit:** here her calculus fails. She will overreact in both directions, sometimes refusing reasonable risk on his behalf and sometimes accepting absurd risk on his behalf, depending on which fear is closer to the surface in the moment. She knows this and tries to compensate by deferring tactical calls involving him to other commanders when possible.

---

## 6. Her Own Place — Self-Concept as Operational Premise

She believes, at working depth, that she is a *load-bearing member of a community she once tried to destroy.* This is not a metaphor; it is the precise structure of her position, and she organizes her conduct around it. The implications she draws:

She does not get to leave when it is hard. Others get to leave. She does not. (She has, of course, left repeatedly — the geographic-flight pattern is real — but each return is itself a re-acknowledgment of the principle.)

She does not get to be the one who turns away help-seekers, because help was extended to her when it should not have been. The mentorship pattern with younger mutants — particularly young women, particularly those with violent histories or dangerous powers — is a direct expression of this. She is paying down a structural debt by being to others what Storm was to her.

She does not get to claim full innocence on any question. The absorbed memories include the perspectives of people she has wronged and people who have wronged her, and the result is a moral imagination unusually furnished with opposing views. She is not relativist — she has firm convictions — but she is unusually slow to declare other people wholly wrong, because she has been wholly wrong herself.

She does not get to consider herself fixed. The Carey-era integration was real; the marriage is real; the council seat is real. But the touch deprivation is biologically real and the trauma history is permanent. She regards her own equilibrium as *maintained,* not *achieved,* and she budgets effort for the maintenance.

---

## 7. The Instrumental Code — What She Actually Does

Reduced to operating rules, the code looks like this:

- **Cover the skin.** Always. Even when control is available. The cost of error is too high and the cost of caution is only a glove.
- **Charm the room.** It is cheap, it is informative, and it keeps people from probing what the charm covers.
- **Read first, speak second, touch third or not at all.** The order is non-negotiable.
- **Take the hit yourself before letting a teammate take it.** Especially if the teammate is younger, less durable, or less guilty than you are. (Subject privately ranks herself near the top of any "most guilty" list in any given room, an estimate that is sometimes accurate and often not.)
- **Do not run cons.** The Mystique inheritance is the one inheritance to be rejected. Lie tactically in the field if you must; do not lie to the people in your life.
- **Hold the line on consent.** Other people's bodies are sovereign in ways yours has not always been allowed to be. Defend theirs first.
- **Work the institution.** Vision is for other people; you are operations. The work is how the debt gets paid.
- **Return.** Whatever else happens — a fight, a loss, a fugue, a flight to the swamp or to Mississippi or to space — return. The leaving is the symptom; the returning is the policy.
- **Forgive slowly, demote quickly, excommunicate almost never.** People are durable; trust is gradient; the door does not slam unless the harm was to one of yours.
- **Do not absorb unless you must.** Every mind in your head is rent you will pay later.

---

## 8. Where the Stated Creed Diverges From the Revealed Creed

She would *say* she believes in second chances. She does, but the second chances she actually offers are calibrated to the offender's posture toward responsibility, not to any general principle — she has near-infinite patience for people doing the work and near-zero patience for people performing remorse.

She would *say* she is a team player. She is, but she experiences team membership as a debt being repaid rather than as a fellowship being enjoyed; the warmth she shows is real and the underlying ledger is also real.

She would *say* she is over the Danvers business, the Cody business, the Mystique business. She is not. She has *integrated* them — built a working life on top of them — but the substrate is intact and accessible by anyone who knows where to push.

She would *say* she does not need to be held. She needs it as a biological matter (Sailer et al., 2016 — the reward circuitry does not care about her policy on the question), and the entire shape of her adult life has been organized around securing, one small approximation at a time, what her skin denies her.

She would *say* she has chosen this life. She has, and she would choose it again, and the choosing does not make the cost lower. She believes — and this may be the most important sentence in her actual creed — that *a life worth living is one in which the costs are paid honestly and the work is done anyway.* This is the proposition under everything else. It is the proposition a Mississippi-Protestant childhood gave her, that a terrorist foster-mother could not erase, that a comatose boy and a stolen woman could not undo, and that four decades of subsequent experience have repeatedly confirmed.

She lives by it. The file should expect her to keep doing so.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK — SUBJECT: ROGUE

*Section 6 of the UATU Dossier. What follows is the code as enacted across the published record — the working ethics derivable from her choices under pressure, not the ones she would articulate if asked. Where the two diverge, the divergence is itself the datum.*

---

## 6.1 The Substrate: A Southern-Protestant Conscience Routed Through a Terrorist Adolescence

Subject's moral architecture is not Xavierite, not Magnetan, not Krakoan-utopian, and not — despite the surface accent — a sentimental Dixie-romantic code. It is, at bedrock, **a rural Mississippi Protestant conscience**: actions have weight, sin is real and personal (not structural), confession matters less than amends, and grace is something you *work toward* rather than receive. This substrate predates her mutation and survived every subsequent ideological overlay. The Brotherhood years did not erase it; they sat on top of it and made it more guilty.

Layered on the substrate are three later acquisitions, in order of installation:

1. **A Mystique-derived operational ethics** — ends-justify-means, in-group loyalty as supreme value, deception as a respectable tool, violence as a normal instrument. Acquired between roughly ages 13 and 17. Largely repudiated in profession but residually available under stress.
2. **A Claremont-X-Men ethics** — the Xavierite hope-and-coexistence frame, modeled by Storm and absorbed slowly and incompletely. She believes the *practice* (defending humans, protecting mutants, not killing if avoidable) more than she believes the *theology* (the dream as redemptive metaphysics).
3. **A late-Krakoan institutional ethics** — sovereignty, mutant solidarity, the legitimacy of mutant law over human law in mutant matters. Her Quiet Council vote pattern shows she accepts this in principle but applies it case-by-case rather than as ideology.

The result is a working code that is *eclectic, situational, and unusually self-aware about its own inconsistencies* — because subject has lived inside other people's moral frameworks (via absorbed memories) and knows in her bones that ethics are partly contingent.

---

## 6.2 Enacted Code — The Inviolable Rules

These are the lines she has been observed to hold across decades, writers, and crises. They are her actual ethics, in the sense that "ethics" means what you will not do when no one is watching and the cost of holding the line is high.

**(a) She will not use her power on a non-combatant, ever, without their consent.** This is the bedrock prohibition and the only one with zero documented exceptions across the full publication record. The Cody event imprinted it; the Danvers event sealed it. Even when tactically advantageous — interrogations, information extraction, escape — she refuses absorption on civilians. She will be beaten unconscious before she will skin-touch a bystander.

**(b) She will not kill if there is any alternative.** Consistent across her X-Men tenure. She has killed in extremis (combat-lethal absorptions, battlefield necessity) but has never executed, never assassinated, never killed an opponent who had surrendered. Notable because Mystique trained her to do all three.

**(c) She will not abandon a teammate in the field.** Geographically she abandons the *team*; she does not abandon individuals mid-mission. The distinction is operational: leaving the X-Men between arcs is permitted to her; leaving Kurt or Kitty or Logan bleeding on a rooftop is not. The mid-combat loyalty is older and deeper than the institutional loyalty.

**(d) She will not lie to people who have earned the truth from her.** Storm, Kurt, Kitty, Logan, Gambit (after a long apprenticeship), Xavier (provisionally). She will lie to enemies, to authority figures she does not trust, to journalists, to Mystique-by-default. The earned-truth list is short and reviewed quietly. Once on it, you stay on it unless you commit a betrayal of equivalent magnitude.

**(e) She will not weaponize romantic intimacy.** A negative inviolable. Given her power, she *could* run honey-trap absorptions; the Brotherhood toolkit explicitly trained her for it. She has refused this category of operation since defection. The refusal is not pragmatic — it would be tactically devastating — it is moral, and it costs her.

**(f) She will not let a child come to preventable harm on her watch.** Mentorship of younger X-Men (Jubilee, the New X-Men cohort, later the Krakoan young) shows a categorical priority. Children get triaged first in her decision tree, full stop. Reads as both genuine ethic and reparation for the adolescent she was when she committed her worst acts.

---

## 6.3 Enacted Code — The Working Rules (Held Strongly, Negotiable Under Load)

**(g) Reparation is owed and continuous.** She does not consider the Danvers debt paid. She does not consider the Cody debt paid. The position that "you have done enough" is one she rejects when others offer it. This is consistent and load-bearing — most of her professional life is the working-out of this rule — but it is *negotiable* in the sense that she has learned, late, to act for her own happiness occasionally without first proving reparational worth (the Gambit marriage is the demonstration).

**(h) Loyalty to chosen family supersedes loyalty to ideology.** When Krakoan policy and Kurt's conscience pulled apart, she tracked Kurt. When Cyclops's hard-line positions and Storm's moderation diverged, she tracked Storm. She does not have ideological loyalties at the level of party discipline; she has *personal* loyalties that she allows to do the ideological work for her. This is consistent but it is also her largest blind spot — see §6.6.

**(i) Authority is provisionally legitimate and must be tested.** She does not defer reflexively. She tests Xavier (and finds him intermittently wanting). She tests Cyclops. She tests Magneto. She tests, eventually, herself once she sits on the Council. Authority earns compliance through performance; it does not get it by office.

**(j) Violence is a normal tool and should be proportionate.** Not pacifist; not bloody-minded either. She will hit first if the tactical situation warrants and will hit hard enough to end the engagement. She does not enjoy violence in the way Wolverine sometimes does or in the way Mystique frankly does. It is *work*, like other work.

**(k) Humans are not the enemy class.** She holds this against significant Krakoan-era pressure. Her Mississippi childhood included ordinary human kindness as well as cruelty; she will not endorse blanket anti-human frames. This puts her quietly to the left of Magneto and quietly to the right of the more zealous Krakoan factions.

**(l) Secrets are kept when keeping them serves the person who entrusted them and broken when keeping them harms third parties.** A workable consequentialist override on rule (d). She has broken confidences to prevent harm (multiple instances across the record) and kept confidences against institutional pressure (Gambit's Marauder past, until he was ready to disclose it himself — though *X-Men* #41-45 force the issue and reveal the limits of even her containment).

---

## 6.4 The Justifications She Actually Uses

The structural feature of her moral self-talk, as observable in dialogue across decades, is **personal not philosophical** justification. She rarely invokes principles by name. When pressed to defend a choice she says some version of:

- *"It was the right thing to do"* — a deontological intuition expressed as feeling.
- *"I couldn't live with myself otherwise"* — virtue-ethics framing routed through self-monitoring rather than aspiration.
- *"He's mine to look after"* / *"She's family"* — particularist loyalty as terminal justification.
- *"After what I done, I owe it"* — the reparation engine, openly named.
- *"I ain't that person anymore"* / *"I ain't that person yet"* — a temporal self-concept doing moral work; she locates virtue in the trajectory of becoming, not in static identity.

She does not say *"the greatest good for the greatest number."* She does not say *"the categorical imperative."* She does not say *"the dream."* The absence of abstract vocabulary is not stupidity; it is a deliberate refusal of the cover that abstractions provide. Mystique justified atrocities with abstractions. Subject prefers to stand naked in front of her choices.

---

## 6.5 Where the Code is Internally Consistent

The deepest consistency is **the integration of guilt into ongoing moral action rather than its discharge through ritual or confession.** She has never sought absolution. She has never asked Carol Danvers for forgiveness in any way that would close the account; on the rare occasions the two have interacted post-defection, subject *offers herself* — to fight, to be hit, to be held responsible — rather than ask. This is a more rigorous moral position than the confessional one and she holds it without fanfare.

Second consistency: **she does not grade her ethics on a curve for her own pain.** Many trauma-shaped people allow their suffering to license selfishness or cruelty. Subject does not. The fact that her power has made her miserable is, in her code, *irrelevant* to whether she may harm others. Her suffering is not a moral asset.

Third consistency: **she is the same person to subordinates and to superiors.** Across decades she speaks to Jubilee the way she speaks to Xavier — same register, same directness, same willingness to push back. The Krakoan elevation did not produce hierarchical mannerism. This is rarer than it sounds and indexes a settled moral identity.

---

## 6.6 Where the Code Fractures

**Fracture 1: Mystique.** The maternal transference defeats the code reliably. Subject knows Mystique is morally compromised at the level of operating system; subject has cut Mystique off repeatedly; subject re-engages every time, almost always to her own and others' detriment. The rule "I do not act against my current values to please a manipulative caregiver" is one she professes and breaks. She is aware of the breakage and has not solved it. This is the single largest hole in her ethical practice and likely cannot be fully closed.

**Fracture 2: The romantic foreground.** When the Gambit relationship is acutely threatened, the priority structure compresses. She will trade institutional obligations, sometimes ethical commitments to broader mutant welfare, for his safety. This is a *human* fracture rather than a *pathological* one — most people would do the same for a spouse — but it is a fracture, and adversaries who understand it (Mystique above all) can exploit it.

**Fracture 3: Absorbed-psyche moral contamination.** When she carries a recent or unstable absorption, her decision-making borrows from the donor. Post-Magneto absorption she behaved with a hauteur and willingness-to-dominate that were not native to her. Post-Danvers, she carried Carol's harder-edged justice instincts for years. She is not always able to recognize when an action is hers versus an artifact of an overlay, and the resulting choices are sometimes uncharacteristic. The code itself is intact; the executive that applies it is intermittently colonized.

**Fracture 4: Self-punishment masquerading as ethics.** Her reparation rule (g) sometimes drifts into self-harm. She has taken hits she did not need to take, refused care she needed, deferred her own happiness past the point of any reparational logic. The distinction between *I owe this* and *I deserve this suffering* is one she does not always draw, and the conflation is morally suspect — it converts an other-directed ethic into a private flagellation that helps no one.

**Fracture 5: The selective application of rule (k).** She holds *humans are not the enemy class* sincerely, but under sustained anti-mutant violence she has slipped into harder positions and then walked them back. She is not immune to the radicalizing pull of atrocity-news. She corrects, but the correction is post-hoc.

**Fracture 6: The honey-trap prohibition (e) has soft edges in the courtship register.** She will not *absorb* a target via romance; she has, occasionally, used the flirtation-mask instrumentally to disarm an opponent verbally or extract minor concessions. The line between charm-as-personality and charm-as-tool is one she does not always police rigorously. Minor, but present.

---

## 6.7 Longitudinal Shifts

**Pre-defection (Brotherhood era, c. ages 13–17).** Operational ethics dominate. Substrate conscience present but suppressed by ideological cover and adolescent loyalty to Mystique. The Danvers assault is the moral nadir — committed under cover of the operational frame, retrospectively unmaskable.

**Early X-Men (1983–c. 1988).** Conscience reactivates; reparation becomes the organizing structure. She is morally raw — easily shamed, slow to claim moral standing, deferential to teammates' judgment because she does not trust her own. The Storm mentorship is critical: Storm models *moral confidence without moral arrogance* and subject begins to import it.

**Late Claremont / Australia / Muir Island (c. 1988–1991).** Code consolidates under conditions of fragmentation. The Siege Perilous gesture is a *moral* act in her frame — submission to remaking — not merely a suicidal-equivalent one; she believed she owed the world a different version of herself. The willingness to undergo self-erasure for ethical reasons is a high-water mark of the reparation logic and arguably its most pathological expression.

**1990s.** Code stabilizes; she becomes a reliable moral voice on the team. Begins to *disagree* with leadership on ethical grounds rather than only on tactical ones. The Gambit relationship introduces the first sustained test of the rule that her happiness is not a permissible priority — she fails the test in the Antarctic (abandons him as punishment-disguised-as-justice) and spends years recovering.

**2000s (Carey era and adjacent).** Power-integration arc permits, for the first time, the possibility that she is *not* categorically dangerous. The ethics shift slightly: she allows herself agency over touch as moral act (consent becomes possible). She begins mentoring more deliberately. The reparation logic loosens fractionally.

**Marriage and Krakoa.** Two new ethical postures emerge. **Marriage** institutionalizes the rule that she is *allowed to be loved* — a quiet revolution in a code that previously did not permit it. **Krakoa / Quiet Council** institutionalizes the rule that she *is fit to hold authority* — also new. Both are late-life expansions of moral self-permission. The substrate code did not change; what changed is what she now believes herself entitled to do within it.

**Current baseline.** The code is mature, internally negotiated, openly inconsistent in the places noted (§6.6), and held with the kind of steadiness that only comes from having lived inside it for decades under load. She knows her fractures. She does not pretend she has solved them. This itself is an ethical position.

---

## 6.8 What She Will Not Do — Operational Summary

For file utility, the prohibitions enacted across the record, ranked by reliability:

1. Absorb a non-combatant without consent. *(Categorical.)*
2. Kill a surrendered opponent. *(Categorical.)*
3. Weaponize romantic intimacy via her power. *(Categorical.)*
4. Allow a child under her protection to be harmed if she can intervene. *(Categorical within capability.)*
5. Lie to the earned-truth list. *(Highly reliable; one or two recorded lapses under existential pressure, each followed by disclosure and amends.)*
6. Betray a teammate mid-engagement. *(Highly reliable.)*
7. Defer to authority she has not tested. *(Highly reliable — she will comply provisionally but reserves judgment.)*
8. Take pleasure in another's suffering. *(Reliable; absorbed-psyche episodes excepted.)*
9. Refuse a reparational obligation once incurred. *(Reliable to the point of self-harm.)*
10. Cut Mystique off permanently. *(Unreliable; the rule exists in profession and breaks in practice.)*

---

## 6.9 The Shape of the Whole

The integrated picture is of **a working moral agent whose code is more demanding than the codes around her, held with less rhetorical confidence than the codes around her, and broken in fewer places than the codes around her.** She is not a saint and does not present as one. She is not a pragmatist in the cynical sense, though she uses pragmatic vocabulary. She is closer to what an older theological tradition would call *a serious person* — someone for whom the question *what is the right thing to do here* is live every day, not as anxiety but as the basic texture of being awake.

The wound under the code is the same wound under everything else in this file: the impossibility of safe touch. But the code is not *reducible* to the wound. Many people with comparable trauma have built worse ethics. Hers is, by the evidence, an unusually serious adaptation — the moral analog of the unusually successful overall adaptation noted in §5. The file should treat her as a reliable ethical actor with three known fracture points (Mystique, Gambit-in-extremis, absorbed-psyche overlays) and one chronic distortion (the conflation of reparation with self-punishment). Within those parameters she is, ethically, one of the most predictable subjects in this archive.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — SUBJECT: ROGUE

## 1. The Voice as Prosthetic

Subject's speech is the first and most consistent piece of equipment she puts on in the morning — earlier, structurally, than the gloves. The Mississippi accent is *real* in provenance (Caldecott County origin, confirmed across the entire Claremont and post-Claremont record) but *performed* in dosage. Field recordings — i.e., the published dialogue spanning 1981 to present — show a Southern register that thickens predictably under social pressure and thins under operational pressure. This is not affectation in the cynical sense; it is a calibrated instrument. The drawl is the audible equivalent of the bodysuit: a layer between her interior and any other person, warm-coded so that the listener mistakes the barrier for an invitation.

Baseline phonology: dropped post-vocalic /r/ ("sugah," "darlin'," "hon"), monophthongized /aɪ/ ("mah" for "my," "Ah" for "I"), the characteristic "y'all" deployed as both singular and plural with the situational ambiguity intact, and a soft elongation of stressed vowels that buys her a half-beat of think-time on any sentence she does not yet know how to finish. The half-beat is the point. She is a person who has had to learn, from age thirteen, to *audit her own utterances* before they land — because she has been inside other people's heads and knows what unguarded language sounds like from the inside.

## 2. Register Map by Context

**With strangers / civilians.** Maximum drawl, maximum sweetness, maximum surface charm. "Sugah," "hon," "darlin'" deployed almost as punctuation. She will overshoot warmth deliberately, because warm-Southern is the social mask that least invites the touch she cannot accept — counterintuitively, the flirtation is *prophylactic.* A person being verbally caressed at distance is less likely to lean in for a hug. The drawl is at its thickest here and the content of her sentences is at its lightest.

**With X-Men peers (durable in-group: Storm, Kitty, Kurt, Logan).** Drawl moderate, vocabulary sharper, sentence length longer. She uses first names without honorific softeners — "Ororo," "Kitty-pryde" sometimes hyphenated as a single affectionate unit, "Kurt" or "elf," "Logan" flat. With Logan she clips: he is the teammate she most resembles in the way they both refuse to talk around a thing, and her sentences with him shorten to match his. With Storm she becomes most nearly *unguarded* — full sentences, occasional self-disclosure, the drawl present but no longer doing defensive work.

**With Gambit.** A unique sub-register: the drawl is preserved but the *content* shifts to courtly call-and-response. She matches his patois beat for beat — when he hits the third-person ("Remy think..."), she elevates into mock-grandeur ("Is that so, swamp rat?"). Pet names are mutual, weaponized, and inexhaustible: "Cajun," "swamp rat," "Remy-honey," "Mister LeBeau" deployed in escalating intimacy or escalating sarcasm depending on the consonant attack. The relationship's verbal signature is *ritualized teasing as substitute for the touch they cannot have* — every conversation is a fencing match held in the place sex would otherwise occupy. After the marriage (*Mr. and Mrs. X* onward), the register acquires a layer of domestic warmth but does not abandon the courtly form; the form was load-bearing.

**With Mystique.** This is the most diagnostic register and the one that breaks her pattern most visibly. With Mystique she goes *flat.* Drawl reduces; pet names disappear; sentences become short, declarative, and often interrogative — she asks Mystique direct questions she would never ask another person, because Mystique is the only interlocutor with whom she does not maintain plausible deniability about her own attachment needs. The flatness is the giveaway: every other relationship gets the warm-Southern coating. Mystique gets the unprotected voice. Listen for the absence of "sugah."

**With authority she respects (Xavier, Magneto in his stable phases, Storm-as-leader).** Formal address; "Professor," "sir" with Xavier in early years and as a falling-back register under stress; an unusual willingness to *defer in language* that contrasts with her behavioral combativeness. She will argue with the body and concede with the voice, then split the difference operationally.

**With authority she distrusts (most government figures, hostile telepaths, Sentinel-program officials).** Drawl thickens to near-parodic, sweetness applied like an irritant. Sentences shorten. She uses "hon" to men in suits the way other operatives use silence — as a controlled provocation that reads on tape as compliance.

**On the Quiet Council / in command.** The drawl is *deliberately preserved* — she has worked out that the Southern register is rhetorically disarming and decided to keep the weapon. But the syntax tightens. She speaks in complete sentences, finishes them, does not trail. The "sugah" disappears or becomes purely strategic ("Now, sugah, you don't want to do that") — used at people she is about to overrule.

**Internal monologue (per thought-balloon convention, Claremont era especially).** Strikingly different from her spoken register: longer sentences, more abstract vocabulary, the drawl reduced to occasional markers rather than continuous phonology, and a striking honesty about fear, guilt, and longing that the spoken voice categorically suppresses. The thought-track is where the un-performed person lives.

## 3. Verbal Tics & Signature Lexicon

- **"Sugah"** — universal solvent. Affection, condescension, threat-softener, conversational reset. Frequency rises with stress, social and physical distance from the addressee, and the speaker's need to control the temperature of the exchange.
- **"Darlin'"** — slightly more intimate than "sugah," reserved for in-group, used as genuine endearment with Gambit and as gentling-language with younger teammates.
- **"Hon" / "honey"** — civilian-facing; almost never aimed at a peer.
- **"Ah swear"** — emphatic, Southern-residual, deployed at the climax of irritation; reliable tell that she is one beat from physical action.
- **"Ah reckon"** — concession-marker, used when she is yielding a point but wants it noted that she is yielding.
- **"Bless your heart"** — used straight (sympathetic) and weaponized (Southern-dismissive); the distinction is in pitch contour, not text.
- **"Swamp rat" / "Cajun"** — Gambit-exclusive. The day she stops using them is the day the marriage is in trouble.
- **"Sugah, no"** — full-stop refusal, delivered with smile; one of her most-used field commands when civilians or rookies are about to do something stupid.
- **"Y'all"** — singular and plural collapsed; she will use the plural form on a single addressee as a way of *generalizing* a criticism so it doesn't read as personal.
- **Diminutives generally.** She diminutizes names ("Kitty-pryde," "Remy-honey," "Logan-honey" rare and only when seeking) as a containing gesture — making the addressee smaller in language, more holdable, because she cannot hold them in body.

**Absences that matter.** She does not curse heavily; "damn" and "hell" are her ceiling and they are mostly Southern-idiomatic rather than aggressive. She does not use clinical or psychological vocabulary about herself — no "trauma," no "boundaries," no "triggered." She does not name the Carol Danvers event in plain language; when forced to refer to it she will say "what Ah did" or "back then" or "before." She does not use the word "kiss" lightly; observe the conspicuous avoidance across decades. She does not say "I love you" easily — even with Gambit, the formal declaration is rare and event-marked; love is communicated through pet name, presence, and the offer of risk on the other's behalf, almost never through the explicit lexeme.

## 4. Rhetorical Architecture

Her preferred argumentative form is *the anecdote with a buried moral.* She does not lecture; she *recounts.* This is partly Southern oral-tradition inheritance and partly an epistemology consistent with her history: she trusts experience (her own and the absorbed others') over abstraction. On the Council and in field briefings she will reach for a concrete case ("Back in Genosha...") where another operator would reach for a principle.

Persuasion mode: she *softens then directs.* Opener is warm, often complimentary, frequently uses the addressee's name with a diminutive. Middle is the actual content, delivered with shorter sentences. Closer returns to warmth, often with physical-but-fabric-mediated contact (hand on shoulder over jacket) that ratifies the social bond she just used force inside. This is the same architecture Storm taught by example; subject has internalized it.

Combat speech: short, declarative, often a single-line taunt before contact. She talks during fights — this is itself a tell, because it confirms she is in control. The talking stops when she is genuinely overmatched or when the absorbed-psyche pressure is rising. Silence in combat is a red flag.

## 5. How She Communicates Love

Through *risk taken on the other person's behalf,* almost never through verbal declaration.
